Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear or the patient dies now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the disease of the mouse according to what we have said in the divisions of cures, and it does not benefit at all, then add three methods of cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Here is the translation of the first sentence:
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	Aprés, I put the two needles inflamed so that the key is perceived from the other side, and then treat the fire cautery, and thus there will be four; if you see, then cauterize the entire cautery at three needles.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when it has gained putridity by long time, and this is true for another of the cures previously said.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery is not worth for dropsy, except in the manner that is called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure according to the manners that we have said in divisions, and your cure does not benefit, then it is necessary that you make four cauterizations around the mouth, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the spleen, and two behind the back on the spine, and one in front of the breast; and let the cauterizations be well close to the space of the key.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After that, let the cauterization remain open to drain impurities for a long time, and do not cease the cure of the patient after the cauterization; and healing will hasten, and both intentions will come together with the aid of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cauterization for the belly is the clavile that we have shown before; and that one for the back is olive-like, according to what is mentioned here before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in one who is dropsical and are full of yellowish water, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and raise your hand with the cautery so as not to turn.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not go too far in, otherwise the yellowish water would burst forth, and make the cautery according to this form:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	Aprés fait two fire cauterizations on each leg, one at the tip of the cutaneous fold and the other below the kneecap in front and behind the leg; let the cauteries be long without healing until the pus is gone; then cure the other cures we have mentioned.
de la menoison	Of the dwelling place
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, as long as the retentive and digestive virtues in the stomach and intestine are impaired, and cannot be cured by any means of cures; and you see the patient suffering greatly and of strong virtue, then make one great cauterization on the stomach according to what has been spoken before about the cauterization of the stomach, at the cauterization of the circle; and four cauterizations around the anus subtle each like a small nail, and two cauterizations on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistures abundant and the patient suffering, then make a cauterization on the navel, and one cauterization on each rib, and two small cauterizations on the stomach below the great one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and are old and consist of large, cold, moist, corrupt humors, and they are cured as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit, if you do cauterization: three on the spine of the back, that which is entirely behind the almond-shaped skin and triangulating, and one cautery below the jawbone two days; and if you think his stomach is chilled, and the meat is not cooked, and the face swells, then one makes a great cautery on the stomach, as said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen at all the cautery's length; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment let the wound heal until it is clean.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	Of the swelling which is called "Thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cope with Thelul, if it seems to be a flaccid cauterization, then apply the cauterized part to the swelling that has been copped; and let it remain as long as the cautery comes to the birth of the vein, so that the blood may not flow; do this once or twice, and if there is much Thelul, then cauterize each one as we have said; after curing with ointments that are beneficial until they are healed; and if you apply a great cauterization on the armpit, it will have greater aid.
de plaie mal curee	Of an unhealed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot bear cutting or opening, as we will tell in its place, then comes a disease that cannot be healed except by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When any fistula comes, and is inflamed and discharges pus and corrupt moisture, so you must prove the entire tent-like thing to be very subtle, and note how deep it goes.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After scaling the cautery that seems rough, and plug it into the fistula according to the amount the tent-like thing has entered, and resume the cautery as many times as there is rotten and corrupt flesh, once, twice, or three times, depending on the quantity of what is needed; and beware of burning the nerves that are nearby, and the great veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the bladder and intestine, then beware of these places, and do not make a fire except on burned skin, and think that it is not perilous; after treating the wound until it is clean, and if the swelling has subsided, and the materials are removed long ago, then know that the swelling is healed entirely; and if the materials are not removed, know that the swelling is trapped, and corrupts the bone at its root; and thus as one of those things we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	Of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes to the kidneys and great flatulence, and does not take shape like a woman's, then it is necessary that you make a cauterization on the kidneys from one side and the other, at the cauterized part like a small nail that we have said before; and if we were to cauterize in the middle, there would be three cauterizations in a line, and they will cause greater aid.
de la vessie	Of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cauterization on the back part of the bladder, where the hairs of the navel begin, and one to the right and one to the left, and let each cauterization be as long as the nail of a thumb; and make one cauterization behind the back, or two if you need them; and let the cauterizations be like small nails according to the form said before.
de la marris	Of the kidneys
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the kidneys are cold and moist, and do not let anything conceive, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends are delayed; and when they come, one feels great pain: then it is necessary that you make three cauterizations around the anus, as we said about the bladder, and two cauterizations behind the back; and let the cauterizations be like small nails, as we said.
de la hainche	Of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous moistures descend to the buttock of the hip, and because of this the patient moves out of its place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when one measures them together; and it is found that the lump of the department vein is there, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the buttock of the hip with a cauterization resembling a circle, and sign in front of the lump around the buttock as it turns, so that the buttock is within the circle; and let the cauterizations be such as those for the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauterizations are not present, then make three great cauterizations on the olivary region, and let the cauterizations be as deep as all the kidneys; and cure until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the buttock of the hip, and it is from coldness and moisture, and the patient is cured according to what we have said in the division, but the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient with pills made from fetid substances, or other good-smelling pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After the fire cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to two manners: that is to say together burning medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is according to many manners, one of which is: that you cauterize on the back of the hollow belly three triangular cauterizations in this form, and make a good depth and size, and have between each cauterization the thickness of an egg, and it should be the olive-shaped cauterization; sometimes one makes a cautery in the middle on the head of the hollow belly, for which there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, apply the cauterize to the fire circle that we have mentioned earlier in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in this way that the circle contains all the hip and all the hairs of the wound are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And that's the manner in which one does it in sciatica, when the pain holds in the back and does not reach as far as the thigh or as far as the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes as far as the thigh and leg, then one makes two cauterizations there where the patient says that the pain is held, and one cauterization on the ankle four digits deep, a little to the left; and the cauterizations should be cutellate, and the thickness of the key should be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends as far as two or three toes away from there, then one cauterizes where they feel the pain three or four points away.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, make another one; and if he knows that the pain is under the knee towards the thigh, make a cauterization at the cutaneous or circular cautery, and take good care in all your cauterizations that you do not leave the cautery so long that you burn the nerves and great arteries, and that you do not cause more harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who have had a fire cauterization on the ankle of the foot, and left them so that the leg was completely swollen, and the feet also, and it was pierced and corrupted all the feet.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a purge of the belly in which he obtained his death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in two parts together, make a cauterization in one and in the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men say in the cauterization of the groin, as to why it is thus, make it such a shape and be at the top just as big as a nutmeg or a little less, and be by intervals and be so many intervals from one to another that they take up the quantity of an egg; and let the intervals be four fingers wide, and also like hazelnuts, and there should be about a fistful of iron well made; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Here is the translation:
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use this cautery because of the fear of his gaze, and if we see little who uses it; and yet this is one of the good cauteries, which can be endured, and where it applies.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cauteries of medicine burning are such that you make an instrument to fit between the edges of the door, and it should be made of clay or iron, one foot long, and in the middle have two notches, and between each notch have the quantity of the thickness of a finger; and they should be overhanging above and below, and come together together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	Put the boiste of the hairpiece on the patient lying on their side, and after that place your hand on top of the boiste of the hairpiece; afterwards pour between the two circles of hot water which has been heated to a boil one pot, and let it leave for an hour or two times, and allow the patient to endure the heat and burning.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it finds an ulcer just like from fire; and when the ulcers have passed, lift up your hand with the instrument and lift off the soft hairpiece of sweet water, and leave thus for three days, and put on butter until what is blackened by scarring is removed; and then let it be left in peace for three days more; and that would be the final aid after the cure of ointments as long as he is healthy.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread to the hip or leg, make the instrument that holds it as you have made in the previous correct manner; and this is the method of hot poultice, and I have written it in the treatise on the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and hot water, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put it in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	Or if there is a small hole to drain what the point of a razor can enter; and put this pot over another well-weighted pot, and place on top alkali and hot water and sweet poultice, so that there will be two above the powders as you have prepared it with your hand; and let it thus until the sweat and juice flow down into the weighted pot, then take all this sweat, and pour it onto hot water and alkali just as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very hot and administered in motion of medical works and other cauteries for members; For it makes a work like fire, and thus to other medicines that one cauterizes well the groin with honey, anacardi, and callosities with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a treatment by which one man was cured of the pain in his groin and sciatic vein, and he praises it greatly, saying that no other treatment was done, and that he was healed at once when this treatment was performed, and he bathed himself as it is taught hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in the same manner that you take a fresh and dry vertigre, and grind it much with a little bit of grease, and put it on the groin, on the thigh, and on the leg where the pain is, and bind it; and let it be for three hours and by the time the patient no longer feels burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter the bath until his body is slightly warmed up, and make him enter the bed, and the pain will go away completely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use a fire cautery for such medicines unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's hair, it helps a lot; and it should be done in this way.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and soak it in old oil, and place it on the hollow that is between the thumb of the foot and the other one called fossicle.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After that take goat's hair that is dry, and set it on fire until it is charcoal, and place it on the linen, and let it stay until it is extinguished; and do it again in this way, and do not stop doing it like this until you think by sense that it will come up to the groin, and that the pain will cease; and this manner of cautery is called "goat's hair cautery".
de la dolor dou dos	from the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling or percussion or excessive blood evacuation, or from something cold and spread out, none of these similarities are worth cauterizing, except for that which comes from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after this that the patient be rid of fetid pills or similar things, and have them applied to the back, where the pain is located, three lines marked with ink, and in each line five cauterizations or more according to virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cautery be done according to the "point" cautery; and if you see fit, do three or four cauterizations at the middle nail-shaped cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often comes to small children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a narrow space between their vertebrae when they wake up, and fear; and you will find it in the lower part of the back and in no other spine.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you want to cure it, then cauterize at the "celcle" cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the fire cautery proceeds evenly throughout each part of the spine.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, then cauterize around the spine with the fire that pricks 2 or 3 lines and have the points close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the cure, leave it so that it is healed according to what we have said, and be careful not to apply cauterization in a gibbous area which is near a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	from the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints is due to moisture that spreads to each limb of the body, and when the pain comes in the feet, which doctors properly call "podagre", and when it is caused by cold matter and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauterization in this manner: make the fire of cauterization around the jointure of the foot, and let it be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need for you to prick on the face of the foot, then let the fire cauterize all over it as we claim "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the knee and other joints, and this happens many times, then let the fire cauterize on each kneecap three or four times, throughout all the olive-shaped part; and if you need more, do more, but don't keep your hand there longer than until the fat of the bone is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, administer the cautery that we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make pricks around the joint II lines; and if there remains no pain to the shoulders, make pricks above each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the ribs or down to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and take good care of the patient and prepare medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you take good care of him and purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the thread of silk
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When itching comes in the armpits, and the boils descend to the groin and it is newly so, then it is necessary that when you see it being cured, that he does not scratch that day; and that he uses things which loosen the bowels, so that the faeces descend from his belly; afterwards make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath until the boils are repaired, and then rekindle at your two hands, and mark with ink below the itching on the bone of the wrist, and at all one sign which is similar to half a circle above the body; then apply the cautery according to this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until he is pale and evacuates stool.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then put the bowels back in their place; and have someone hold his hand so that they do not return behind; and take good care of the patient's hips, and put a cushion and a servant under him on the hips, and another one above the breast which holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign of all your hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, do it again as many times as necessary to reach the bone; and beware subtly that the bowels do not move when you are doing the cautery, nor burn him; and thus the patient will not die or suffer from another evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come close to the bone at the cautery, your efforts are worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is fitting that the cauteries of children are subtle according to their measure, and those of great people also great according to theirs; after three days' care, grease the place where the cautery was done with butter until the scabbing is removed; after caring for other ointments until they are healed, and have the patient sit on his back for 40 days until the wound is well closed; and it is fitting that their bedsores be relieved for a long time, so that the boils do not burst when he needs to go into chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after 40 days, when he wants to get up, let him be given a well-made bandage, and wear it for another 40 days; and have good rest, so that he does not work too little and take care of excessive drinking and eating, and shouting too loudly; and when he follows this instruction, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say afterwards the treatment of cutting in this chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	from the itching of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ulcers come to other bellies and are recognized, and you see they no longer grow, then make the fire cautery of fire according to its quantity, and let it burn the third part of the skin; afterwards do the cure as we have said; and some of the ancients have said that one should cauterize at the cautery with three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but mark the first line of the flesh and make a line above the ulcer for its width, and another below, and stretch your hand through all the cautery nail.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are lighter and more subtle.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	from old pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any member, whether from falling or striking, and that pain lasts for a long time, and the cure of medicine is not worth it, then it is necessary that he be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and let the cauterization be according to the length of the member, its smallness, weakness, virtue, and location of twists and pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed from the first cautery, that's good; if not, begin another one on top of it, for these cases are such that they should be moved to the member that is closest, so you must make the cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	A wound
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The members are helped sometimes by cautery with great help, and similarly the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can't you see him being cauterized, take care if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not settle or remain, and you doubt that the corruption will consume all of the patient, then make V cauterizations on his head: one inside the head nine times, and the other towards the forehead to the end of the eyebrows; and two on each horn, and one behind on the back; and leave your hand there until the cautery comes down to the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can issue forth; and cauterize on the nose according to what it is beforehand.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the wound is spread out everywhere; and it is manifestly failing, then it is necessary that you cauterize those cauteries on the head that we have said, and one on the neck, and two on the spine of the back, and six on the spine of the back, and one great one on the crupie and another below, and two on each shoulder; and two on the sides, and two on the tendons of the breast, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and take care of the nerves that are on the backside, lest you burn them; and at times make a cautery on the bone of the elbow, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And knows that when I do more cauterizing, the more help it is, and brings greater benefit; and knows that the patient does not feel pain from cauterizing as healthy people do, because the body is already fully corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is fitting that the cauterizing be great and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the cure, wash the wound with flour mixed with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When inflammation comes to any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and poultices, and it is not healed, then make cauterizations on the member according to its size and smallness; and let the cautery be a little deep into the fat of the skin; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes one makes a cautery at the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the member, and thus if it is removed the swelling; and yet no one intervenes unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the nerves moving in the body.
de albaras	of ulcers
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "ulbaras" is inflamed, and the art of medicine does not do anything, then cauterize it with one cautery, a little deep, according to the quantity of the flesh of the bone, until the whitish color is removed, and its color is changed; then cure with a mixture of flour and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of colt and blood of alder, each in equal parts; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and apply it to the wound until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the cure for chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre comes at the beginning, and you want to arrest it, then cauterize it with the cautery that seems like a circle, all around the border of the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet the wise say that one should make a cautery in the middle of the chancre; and yet this does not seem to me good, for I fear it may be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen sometimes; and more rightly is it that it should be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circle", as we have said about many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of swelling that cannot be cured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When some person has a disease called "adubelati", and it tars to kill or by the superfluity that it makes or by the age of the sick person when he is decrepit (that is, too old) and he has little blood, or by the season; and you see it hastening to kill: then cauterize him with many small cauteries in poking; after that leave him thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing all the way through the entire cautery, then heat the cautery until it has the shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the midst of that disease which is called "adubelati" until the cauteries have pierced the core, and be such cauteries that the patient feels them outside in such a way that the course of purging is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterward take care of him until he is perfectly well.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cure by fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of disease is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a consumption of member, for it consumes the members just as fire consumes dry straw.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a place that can endure cautery together with fire, then sharpen the cauteries little and large, according to what is needed for the place where the disease is; after that, cauterize all parts so that you root out all corruption, and leave nothing behind, that everything that is corrupted be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let it be for three days, and put on the cauterized areas a poultice suffering with oil as long as the burn marks from fire are removed, and all corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of ointments generates flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, it is good; and if not, then restart the cauterization on what remains of the corrupted areas.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this remedy has been sometimes cured with medicinal water in place of fire cauterization; but however, fire cauterization is of greater aid, and I have already said the treatment of medicinal water in the section: take what you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of corns that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Much of a time it happens that in the feet due to outside things a disease is born which is called "clos" according to our intention, and it is a large ugly thing that hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterization of this disease is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	It means to know fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is when you shape the cautery like a vulture's beak from good iron to the measure that it can penetrate the nail from all sides and have subtle edges; after that, you put it all hot on the nail, and turn your hand entirely around the nail until it comes to the head of the nail; and then leave it thus for three days until it begins to suppurate; then apply a poultice of wild meadowsweet bruised with oil, and let the poultice be on all night, and the nail will fall off and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the joint with oil anointing it as long as it is sound.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by outward signs of the body, and many times happen in hands and feet, then it is necessary that you apply hot water cautery; and this is how: take an earthen or iron tube, or a goose quill, and place it on the boil and the abscesses, that is to say, pustules; and put the tube so that it encircles all around, then put in a little of hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the margin of the tube comes to the root of the boil, and thus the hot water can penetrate deeply to the root; and let the patient suffer a little from the burning of the hot water for an hour; then leave it like that, and it will be dislodged completely at all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Soften one after another, as you reach all those inside the body, then treat the swellings that produce flesh.
li cure dou trembler	And the shaking cure is this: take a small piece of bread and butter it, then give it to the patient to eat, and as soon as they have eaten it, they will stop shaking.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some shake due to cold or numbness, or quartan fever or another, it is necessary that you make four or five cauterizations on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each spine; and one on the belly, and one on the stomach at the olive-shaped cauterization; so the shaking will cease, and the patient's health will hasten from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	Of foul pustules: take a piece of linen cloth and soak it in warm water, then apply it to the affected area, keeping it there until the pus is drawn out; afterwards, dry the wound with another piece of linen.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes appearing on the outside of the bathed body or pustules stinking, that come from large corrupted matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	So it is necessary at the first sign when they appear that one makes a fire cauterization on each head of the pustule: a subtle cauterization of myrtle wood, so that the point is seized by fire, or of long aristolochic root, or a lenticular cauterization.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes when one cauterizes at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow further forward, but the superfluities that come are broken off and cleansed; but it is necessary for this to be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut: take a piece of cloth or linen and apply it to the wound, binding it tightly with a string or thread, so that the bleeding may stop; then, if there is still some bleeding, you should make a cauterization on the edge of the wound with hot iron, in order to seal the artery.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there occurs great bleeding from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the surface, or at the incision of an abscess, or at the cauterization of a member, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when this happens to anyone, if you hasten to place your two fingers on the wound of the vein, and press hard until the blood is stilled under your fingers, and no more flows; then take a few small or large cauterizations, all red with fire, and take one, great or small according to the wound and its location where the artery is severed, and place it on that vein where you are holding your fingers, and hold the cauterization there until the blood is staunched.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it starts bleeding again when you lift your fingers from the vein, and the cauterization has cooled, then take another one of the hot cauterizations hastilly.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this one after the other until the blood is staunched; and take care that you do not burn the nerve which is nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be well staunched unless by one of the three ways we have said: or by cauterization, or by extraction if it is not already treated, or by a tight bandage with thread, or by medicines applied which have the power to stop bleeding; and let it be bound and restrained in due order.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever applies binding tightly with cloths or puts hot things on, or similar things, will not benefit if it is not done skillfully.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he does not have a surgeon or medicine available, then he should place his two fingers on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press hard until it is staunched above the wound and above the vein; and do not move it, but wet it with cold water often enough that it is very cold, so that the blood is congealed and thickened and staunched; and make enquires ahead for what he needs in terms of cauterizations and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book of surgical remedies.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases for which it is necessary to use fire cauterization or hot medicine, and the uses, causes, and forms of cauterizations; and I have placed that chapter from head to foot, and I will go on with this chapter in the same way so that one may more easily find what they seek.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And therefore, dear friend, it is necessary that you learn that in this chapter there is more peril and fear than in the first of cauterizations, and for that reason it is necessary to be on greater guard.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many types of people come seeking cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from those who are so tormented by their illness that they will die quickly due to the ferocity they find in their disease, and the great wickedness of their illness; and one should fear these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And there are those who give you their senses, and say: "Wait, I am healed"; and the illness is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting for you to consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put greater caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not act foolishly but wisely concerning what you are certain of and can take and hold; and use prediction and indication in the cures of your patients so that salvation may be converted; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, glory, and praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear friend, May God give you a good understanding and direction, and if you wish to be inspired by the holy breath of His hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	And now I have completed this chapter as I outlined it by chapters, according to what is before the chapter on cauterizations, which I outlined from head to foot, so that you may more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The full-blooded water chief
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness often comes to children at birth, and when the midwife strains too tightly on the child's head; and sometimes it comes from a known cause or not.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness occur except in children, and all those that I have seen died from it; and for this reason it seems to me that one should hasten the work less in such cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose head was full of water, and the head grew bigger each day until it could no longer be borne; and it swelled so much that it seemed dead, and this swelling is gathered beneath the bone above the forehead, between the skull and the bone; and the work is such if the moisture is between the skull and the bone, and the abscesses are small, that you cut a slit in the head as wide as two fingers; and be just as long as two nostrils, until the moisture runs; and look at the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen and the abscesses are larger, then make two cuts in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and you see signs that the commissures of the head are opened on each side, and the water jumps forth when you press it with your hand from within, and this is not responded to: then it is necessary that you make three cuts in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture away.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After applying poultices and powders, put vinegar and oil on it, and let it be like that for five days; then release it, and treat the wound with tents and ointments, and let the head drain equally, and thus feed the patient dry meat without moisture until the member is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at where the abscess opens, and the gathering of the water; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes to the right; and sometimes to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then at the place where the abscess opens, and the gathering of the water, and the vein according to what you have the power to do; and beware that you do not cut the artery; and come forth a stream of blood, so that the patient may die from the loss of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of rheum
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone a disease which is called "cough" in the sides or at the breast, and the disease is old, and medical treatment does not help, then the last resort is the fire cauterization with what one will cut off the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is then necessary, when you are covering the wounds, that the patient makes his head rear; after which rub the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then have the patient pull back his neck to the entire cloth; then look where the vein beats, and the pulsations of one and the other are behind the ears, and they are responsive; then mark the pulsation by incision, then cut one and the other with a sharp spathula-like instrument for two parts, until the flesh comes down to the bone, and this should be done by the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, put the spatula under the artery and cut above it, cutting in the same way as two fingers pass through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, then blood sprays high continuously forth.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Et if the artery does not open to sensing, so it is necessary that you measure the quantity of the space three fingers deep, then sign and fill just to the bone; and what it is necessary to do about blood putting forth is six cubits, and by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can suffer, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone point the syphac, so cut off that apostemes come not there, then strain the wound and tie, and the ointment cure until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old migraine comes, and sharp cough, due to the moisture of tears and heat in temples and old forgotten habits and similar things, and it is not helped by medical treatments or any remedies, then we cut off the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient makes his hair on temples go back, and feels for the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its pulsation, and is hardly responsive except in some men who are too cold; and if it is responsive, then the patient stretches his neck with certain cloths, then rubs the place with a rough cloth, and applies hot water to the place until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula of which this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then treat it above the ligaments, and depart well from the fibers that are below each part; and if the artery is subtle, so turn it to the point of the thread, then cut off that part according to the quantity of two joints.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Since she is not cut, the blood does not flow entirely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And treat the blood of .vi. c/ up to .iii.; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a double thread of strong silk, so that no pus forms before the wound is sewn shut and bleeding stops; then cut off the excess flesh that is between the two ties at the same hour, and then, if you see, cauterize the area with a cauterizing knife down to the bone until the skin is cut; and this is the main work, if the patient has no fever and has a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For fire cauterization is aid to finish off the moisture; that's why it is of greater help for moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the wound with old cotton and places a tent well made on top; and when one removes them, there should be care taken to apply dry medicines that produce flesh, and tents, until he is healed; and if there is no chance of getting hold of the artery so far as you are working, then hasten to cauterize with fire, or fill the wound with vitriol and strain it with your hand so that the blood is stopped; and if you do not have what is present, then put a cloth on the wound so that the blood congeals, and rub the wound with cold water until the bleeding ceases, and be strained as needed; and what is most important and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein with this fire-cutting instrument in two parts, but the cutting should be well spaced to keep their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	Because when the instruments are too tight, they retain less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two knives a space of a finger's breadth, and then when you have signed off on both sides, and you place the hot iron on so that it reaches to the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and let them be separated between the two shoulders because it is not sewn with this cautery from head to foot; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.
