Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an enchanted abscess, and I will come to the treatment of gangrene after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the wound is over
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from a cautery of wound or fissure of syphilis, and it is on the belly and in some of the bowels, as it happens in other ulcers, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from windiness; and if this is due to the rutting of syphilis and the issue of the bowel, then the color of the aposteme is similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and clear of diverse issue.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is from the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses on the belly so that it rebounds, and then returns, and by chance becomes hardened, and greatly enlarges at the entrance to the bath and through strong labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is because of moisture, then it is a light thing, and clear when you press on it with your hand, and do not constrain it; and if it is because of blood, then it appears by these signs, the aposteme being large and hard, and fixed according to a quantity; and if it is because of windiness, then it is soft to the touch, and the work is that you observe whether the appearance is due to the blood from the artery, or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	You should leave the treatment alone.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, about the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the bowel, then you should instruct the patient to hold his abdomen, and be stretched out straight, then sign around the belly; then command him to sit patiently between your hands, then go around the place where you have signed, all the way to the pubic region; then open half of the abscess above all the great unciform bone; then tie it around with a strong thread or cord firmly, and let the abscess be dissolved; then work on the opened half above the thread, and push out your finger, and release the intestine; if you find that it is caught by the thread, then release it, and push the intestine back into the belly; and if you find the bowel, then take hold of it with the unciform bone, and cut away any superfluity; and if the artery or vein makes opposition, then go around carefully, then return to your work and take two needles, and stick two strong threads on them, and tie the two needles around what you have done in a cross shape that you would pierce; then strain the abscess in four places above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place as long as it can be left, and cut away dead flesh by itself; or you may cut it when it is subtle and porous, then treat the wound as needed, and dissolve the abscess as we have said; and extract any blood or moisture that you find, then treat the wound as needed, and bind the wound.
dou chancre	of the sore
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division about the similarities of sore, and how one should work it with medicines, and how one should avoid the cure by fire; and say that the sore should be left to itself in the marrow, and great caution is needed in the cure. And the old ones say that when sores are in a place or can be reached as if they were in the very bones, and in the hips, and in similar places, you must entirely remove it when it starts; and when it is large and old, do not approach it, for I never saw one cured; nor has anyone before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place or can be removed as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile at some point; then make him healthy if he has manifest repletion; then prepare the patient one good place to do the work; then take your needles or sore and clean it from all sides, and remove it from all sides without leaving anything behind; and let the blood run freely and press well the place with your hand or something, and if the flow of blood makes you resistant to the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize as long as the blood is flowing; then cure with another cure until he is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have spoken of the similarities to dropsy in the division, and how the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is done through medicines, and that which is cured through iron: it shines solely; and one should not touch with iron in these two similarities: that is to say, tympanites and ypopsarche, for it is a mortal thing; therefore, when you are treating this similarity of dropsy called "eclites" by medicines, and the cure does not profit, then look to see if the patient is weak, or if he has another disease than dropsy, such as wind and similar things; then do not touch with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient to be of strong virtue, and he has no other disease but dropsy solely, and he is neither too young nor too old, then thus proceed: lift the patient up straight on your hands, and the attendants press the belly out pushing water down to the lowest part of the stomach, then take the spatula with spikes according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be cut into two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And let it be cut at a point, and yet not so deep that it can reach the intestine when you insert it; and do not damage it. Then look to see if dropsy has spread towards the intestines: if so, then cut upwards on both sides of the belly, three digits from below, starting from the navel. And if it is due to liver disease, then make the incision on the left side of the belly, three digits; and if it is due to the bladder, then make it on the right, and do not let the patient lie on the incision so that fluids do not flow to that weak spot. Then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and stop up, and lift your hand all along the spatula-like piece between the skin and the fatty tissue just as when trimming a fingernail or around; then pierce the fatty tissue until it comes to the eighth part, and that is the water's way, then remove the instrument and this tool has taken its form.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a silver chain, and is of earth or of light stone, and has in the part below a small pit; and on one side three pits, and two on the other side, and one on another; and the shoulder is shaped like a quill, and this is the form of the incision which writers shape their quills.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is the alkali, so that when the instruments come to water, they now descend on the instrument; then empty it one-third or two-thirds, because if you empty more than it's necessary at that hour, by chance the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit from the arm, or he falls powerless, or he approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of his strength, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's virtue signify, and his pulses; then take the instrument and retain the water, and it is retained now for the reason which stops the pit that is on the shoulder, of which I have spoken, so that you pierce in this manner; then recommence the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and take from the water a small quantity; do this some days, and beware of overflowing as long as there is but a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the patient and leave much water, then cure him with hot sand or gravel; and by sweating or bathing in the sun, and drinking; and apply cures of drying medicines until he is healthy; and cauterize on the stomach, liver, and spleen after draining the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born without a small ulcer on their penis, or the ulcer is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it so happens that he must pierce through to all the subtlety very much according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put on the penis a thin cloth of linen, and bind it and keep it like that for three days or four, and when he wants to urinate, if the cloth is opened and he makes urine, then put it back on; and by chance there is no harm, because the urine that comes out does not leave the cloth closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	That which belongs to the cow with the small pore is a small amount of medicine from the cloth of flax, as we have said, if it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the pore in its place are blighted, for none are born with a pore at the head of the penis, therefore they cannot urinate unless they lift their penis high; and they cannot defecate because the matter cannot come to the margin, and this is an evil disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of treatment is that the patient lies on his back, and then lifts the head of the penis and cuts it similarly to the shape of a feather, so that the foreskin can open in its place, as it should; and take care of the bleeding which comes many times, and if it happens, stop the bleeding with what stops blood, and cure the wound until he is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	These blisters often come on the penis, and it is a foul appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so you should take them with a very fine needle, cut and scrape all of them away, then put on moist cotton in Egyptian ointment; then cure with divine ointment until he is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the bathwater is malignant, of bad color and smell, then you must apply a cauterization there.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it open, and the bathwater is in the penis, and has part within the skin and part outside, then you must remove the bathwater that is inside first; and when it is sealed, then care for the part outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Car when you treat it together, if the head of the penis is not assured that it will not be pierced, and there comes blackness and corruption in its head and in its sheath; so it is necessary to remove all that is black and corrupted, then lay on the plaster of honey and flour which is made from the rind of green apples and vetches, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding comes from it, so apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery is helpful in two dispositions together: that is to say, in the bleeding of blood and in the corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, so it is necessary that you boil or lead the penis with a piece of cloth, and have the patient urinate between; and when the hair is grown at the head of the penis which has not been circumcised, whether it be due to a wound or an abscess, so it is necessary then that you circumcise it with a sharp instrument, as long as the ligaments are loosened, and the head of the penis is freed from all parts; and if this is a difficult thing to do, so it is necessary that you circumcise it with a small papyrus or piece of linen moistened in cold water, which will not reattach itself again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the removal of continuity as are other wounds; however, when we do this work at our own will and properly for children, it is necessary that we make the best work and the easiest for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancient ones did not instruct their children in circumcision, for they do not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greatest part of the masters and physicians who perform circumcision around a piece of linen, with forceps, and all in one new cloth; it was necessary to cut through because there are two skins, and by chance if you cut above and leave that below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	And then it is necessary to cut again, and there is double pain, and the point of the member is not assured by the mundification; and at the mundification of the wound by chance the iron escapes, and the work is spoiled, and many times it happens that they do not need mundification and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the mundification which is done with forceps throughout all the ligament of thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forceps cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you press your hand, so that it is equal on all sides; but make sure the boy is well wrapped around the skin; and the manner of the first work is such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are not making him swallow more than just tying the thread around the rod as much as possible, and then letting it hang in all ways you can; then let it rest between your hands straight up and down, and reposition the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see it, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the rod and blow or cool it, and treat it above until the head of the rod is inserted; then cleanse it well of the dirt that is assembled there, then tie the signet with a double thread, then tie it under one link to another; and hold it by two strings at the second bond pocket and knee indicator, and cut between the two links, then lift the cord above hastily and treat the head of the rod; then let the blood flow slowly, for this is the purging; and put powder on top and top with powdered drapeau glued from a cooked egg yolk mixed with rose water, oil roset good and fresh, and leave it on until the next day, and cure it with another cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forceps for mundification is this: the two jaws should be held and should be cutting, and should be the same size as each other.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	the error of the mundification is when the iron within flows into the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your finger, so that the ligament makes an abscess; and cut evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then hold it with forceps, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it lasts for three days, and what is below the penis becomes inflamed, then let it be so until the abscess is pacified, and then scrape it lightly; then cut as you can move, and take care of the part of the penis, it will not harm anything.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat then the wound of sudden powder that we have spoken about in dealing with powders, and if one cuts too much beyond measure, and it goes above, so as not to harm; treat it then as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of urine.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	Li retenue of the urine is of stone, or blood congealed, or bowel, or newborn flesh, or similar things that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see the retention due to the stone which is lodged in the back or navel of the bladder, then it is necessary for the patient to be bent over his knees; and his feet should be placed on the back, and he should stretch his belly from the part above the back, and restrict the patient's movements as much as possible; and then the neck of the bladder will be constrained by the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary for you to administer extraction with all the instruments which are called "siringue", whose form is: and be of silver, subtle, light, feathered like a bird's comb; and be about half a palm long, and subtle at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	Et the manner of issuing urine is that you take a doubled thread, and tie it at the chief of a piece of wool or cotton, and put the chief of the thread into the syringe; and remove the superfluity of the wool and put it just to the chief of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and yolk of egg, and make the patient sit on a seat, and raise the bladder and the penis with moist oil and olive oil and dry water; then put the syringe lightly into the penis, until it comes to the root of the penis, then double the penis upwards towards the mouth; then put the syringe forward just to the bladder, and make the patient come just to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order unless because the guide or conductor is twisted; then straighten the thread all along the wool piece and piece, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it further, and make the urine flow; and repeat the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient be eased.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When fluxes or blood come into the bladder, or putridity is assembled, and you see waters and medicines dripping, then make use of all the instruments called "clepsedre", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	She is closed, and if she has three holes: two from one side, and one from the other, as you see; and the leeches shave because the medicine must be such that it stops well the flow without addition, so that one can draw out the moisture, and put when necessary; and when you see your medicines going into the bladder, place the head of the clyster in the moisture, and pull on the pulling string which is inside; then you will pull out the moisture to the clyster, and then push strongly on the pulling string inside; then the moistrors will enter, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the subtle form of the clyster with which one clisters the bladder: thus.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or of archaut, and the head is higher; and below to one side or the string falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the moisture that you see clisterizing the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts with a good double thread, and warm the pot containing that moisture on the fire; then push the head of the clyster into the vulva, then strain your hand on the bladder until all the moisture has gone naturally, so that the patient feels that that moisture has reached the bladder; and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make it a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then push the thread strongly into those holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a dale, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, by pressing your hand until the moisture flows to the bladder.
de la piere	of stone.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the manners of stone, and extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone in the reins, and all signs, and which stone one should work on in size; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you plainly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is in the bladder in children happens more often than in grown-ups, and it's a sign that the water jumps from the bladder like water in its subtlety; and it appears hairy, and greases the patient's penis, and makes him go many times, and then becomes inflamed; and many of these stones fall to the ground; and children's healing is much lighter until they are three years old, and it is very grievous in old age, and it is in middle-age men, between youth and old age; and the cure is more gentle for those who have large stones than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient with a purge, in order to draw out all the foulness that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hinders seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and throw him down and move him to the underside, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes falls from high up; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands be below his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely declining downward; then seek and touch inside; if you feel the stone in position, then hasten now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it doesn't fall at the touching from all, then moisten your thumb with oil from your left hand, if the patient is infirm, or your middle finger, if the patient is youthful and complete; and pour it into its foundation, and seek the stone, and when you feel it on your thumb, then guide it to the neck of the bladder; then press on top of your thumb, and pour it out at the back where you see fit to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the servant to press the bladder with his hand, and tell him to stretch out with his right hand the fingers above, and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the fingers in the part where you are doing the cutting; then put the spatula copant, which is the form.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make between those who is between the cleft and the foundation, not in the middle but on the left side of the left flank; and it should be straight above the stone, and both thighs should be at the foundation, and the width of the traverse should be so that it is large enough to push through, and inside narrow, according to the size of the stone, nor too great; in case the pressure from the thigh which is on the foundation, causes it to jump forth with little effort; and know that there are some stones where there are angles, and margins: then it is hard to exit; and if there are those who are smooth, like a slope, and rounded, whose issue is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And so, when there are angles and margins, make the width greater; and if it doesn't jump forth, then you should pull on the pincers that are like a file at the top, in order to strain the stone so it doesn't escape; or you may push below the I instrument, curved at the top; and if you cannot manage it thus, then enlarge the perforation, and if the sand falls off, then constrict with vitriol; and if there are more than one stones, then push first the largest onto the belly of the bladder, then cut on top, then pull forth, and the small ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then it must be cut out, and a larger wound made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes out immediately because the wound cannot heal; but nonetheless strive to pull it apart with tongs, or to break it up into pieces as much as you can; and when you have completed your work, then fill the wound with incense, aloe, and dragon's blood, and bind it tightly, and apply a wet cloth over it in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, in order to soothe the hot aposteme; then revolve the patient on his back, and do not release the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you release him, then arise the patient very well from oil and water, then anoint him with diaphrenic ointment and basilicon ointment, until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot apostemes come to the wound and corrosion, and congealment of blood in the bladder, and it is retained by this means, causing the urine to back up like that without flowing with the urine: then put your finger into the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and harm it; then lift the wound with water and vinegar and salt, and help him in all the ways you know, until he is healed; and it is necessary that all the works you do to cure him, that you bind his two buttocks together, and assemble the medicines on the bandage.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra of the penis, and stuck inside, and the urine cannot come out; so do as I say, that you cut it many times, or excuse yourself from cutting due to this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I already have this proven thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod according to this form and be fixed at three angles in one fire:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and wrap it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot come further into the bladder; then insert the forest (or point) of the instrument lightly into the penis until you reach the stone; and turn the forest back to your hand bit by bit, as much as you can pierce the stone from the other side; and soon the urine will come out, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is then broken and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this for any reason that hinders it, then take one thread under the stone and another above, then make the penis meet the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and loosen the string, and clean up the congealed blood that is in the wound; and care for it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	Of women's stones
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It often happens that stones are imprisoned in women, and if it ever does, then the cure is grievous, and is prevented by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a well-informed woman who bares herself to mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the husband of the woman is more skilled than the husband of a man, therefore it is necessary to make a deeper cut, and there is great fear. And if necessity requires it, you must take a wise woman who knows, and find one who can be found, or not finding one, then do not hurry I will cast a subtle mire; and present a wise midwife in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command with the examination of the stone; and look very well if the woman is a virgin: then it is necessary to put her dowel or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, then constrain it below her dowel, and recommend that she put her dowel or with the patient, and squeeze and press her left hand on the bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, so it is necessary that she moves it gradually from the entrance of the bladder to below, until it comes to the root of the hip; then cut on the stone at the root of the hip against the middle of the cunny, there where it is most appealing, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her thigh above or below the stone, and make the first incision small; then insert the rod into the incision, if you sense the stone so close to the wound as the stone can issue forth, and know that many kinds of stones are: namely, small and great and rough and smooth, long and round, and those with ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the likenesses to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood swells, put vitriol powder on the place and hold it for an hour until the swelling subsides; then return to your work, as long as the stone is forth, and have the instruments that I told you in the extraction of stones from men to aid you in your work; and if the blood swells, and it is from the artery that was cut, put powder on the place and strain through tents and cloths, and do not start again with those things, and leave the stone alone and do not touch it at all, lest by chance the patient would die; then care for the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of blood is appeased, and the swelling subsides, then return to your work, until the stone is exhausted.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Wet white sac is nothing other than a gathering of moisture or white siphac, which is below the skin of the testicles, that contains the egg; and it is called "siphac", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that it is another egg; and it's the skin of the testicle between the white siphac that we have said; and this does not happen unless it is so.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this wetness is from weakness that comes to the testicles, and spreads this matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, and ceste moistor si a maintes colors: or ce est color declinans a jaunice, or ce est sans rouge, or noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; and ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper cloth, then the abscesses are connected with a part of the yolk, and therefore one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white sac, you will know well; thus when you wish to know the color of the moisture, try all around the quarter circle, so that the form is as before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, what comes after the outline, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we cut by fire, it is necessary that the patient be nourished according to his strength and the replenishment of his body; then place linens on his back, above something a little high, and put cloth underneath him in great abundance; then sit beside him, and command the minister to sit on the right, and stretch out the rod to one of the two sides of the skin of the testicles; then take the spatula left, and cut through the skin of the testicles from long to short until you reach the finger, and make your incision entirely straight as you cut through the skin of the testicles up to the white sac, and scrape subtly according to his strength; then pierce the sac plain with water at a large perforation, and extract all the water, and then put in poultices, and set the sac on top; and do not touch the skin of the testicles but only the sac; cut out or by pieces likewise the edge of it subtly, so that if you do not cut well enough, the water will return; and if the yolk jumps away from your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work on the sac; then assemble the two leaves of the skin of the testicles into a seam, and then cure it as with other wounds, until he is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary that you loosen the vessels that are suspended, doubting the corruption of blood; then cut the testicle to the whole suspensory part, and extract the egg, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the water is assembled into two parts together, know that these are two layers; if you cut the other part as you have made the first one even, then dry the blood, and put in the wound a moist linen cloth soaked in rose oil; and put outside another moist linen cloth soaked in wine and oil, and place on top of the two coins, and place above double cloths, and bind it all together with the cord which is according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths and fill them with wool according to this resemblance and have them sewn together in the girdle of the breeches, and one of the corners take up to the foundation just to the back, and the other to the part of the pointing; and the other chief on top of the two armpits, and be all assembled in the restraint in the buckle of the braier; and sometimes this wick is medicine in lieu of iron cutting, and it's that you take a subtle surgical cauterizer, and cut the skin of the coins, and be heated as we have said, so that the white scurf that contains the water is uncovered; then take the cauterizer according to this form, and pierce that scurf at the nodules, and scrape it with this hot surgical cauterizer.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cautery in all ways that you can, until you reach the end; and beware that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more safe; and carefully guarding against hemorrhage, and watching over the works of surgery; and if anything makes you go against it, whether abscess or hemorrhage or something else, take care of what makes you go against it, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to wait for this work due to its horror, then administer perforation, as I tell you, and know that when you are certain by the signs we have said that the abscess is gone, make the patient sit on a light siege; then pierce the abscess in the part below all the spatula wide, and place the perforation from long of the body; and let it be large holes so that all the water runs forth; then put cotton on the site, and tie it, and leave the remaining water to run, then cure until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow water to issue from the mouth of the wound, then it is necessary that you insert a pin or the instrument with which one treats the water of those with dropsy, as it was before described; and enlarge the poultice on the wound, and know that the water returns, and is assembled after six months or so, and when it is assembled like before, and thus the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the coils
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the cutting of this vein there is fear and many preparations, so it seems to me that it is better to leave it as it is; and I will tell you the work and similar things about the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come to the body, and even to the testicles; and this is by many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to be known by excessive sweetness and humidity, which spreads to the groin, or from percussion; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and there is no pain, and it is a grievous abscess; and by chance some grievous abscesses are fearful and stony, and of faint color, and sometimes comes from a vein or swelling of the artery.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from a vein or artery, it can be known by the hot abscess appearance when you press it with your fingers; and it does not seem right that you should touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made from swelling of the vein is known by its appearance at the expression of the finger touch; and one can well make an incision above this resemblance, and above the other veins; and it is that you should cut away the fat from the groin, then lift up the scrotum, and treat the suspensory ligament of all parts of the scrotum.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the wound is already sealed with these wounds, then you must try to open the wound and the scab; and if it is stuck on the syphilis or in what is inside the vessels, then you must release all that tension and resurface again.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the knot is at the end, then it is necessary that you cut it all and extract the coil, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, then apply the wound with a linen cloth soaked in rose oil and wine, then cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the coils
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping like a bunch of grapes, with the softening of the fibers; and the patient complains grievously when they go; and the cure for this disease is just as fearful as the previous one, and yet we will tell you how to do it, according to what the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then bind the suspensory fibers of the testicles down to your hands, to all the vessels that are close to the penis, and take hold of them, and stretch them out; then cut through the scrotum, cutting wide around the traverse in the direction of the vessels, so that they are uncovered, and then scrape away from each side, just as we have said about extracting arteries that are in the temples; then stick a needle where it has double thread, and tie it to the first point where the vein came out, and tie it again at the other end; then cut through in mid-portion correctly, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupt moors; then treat the wound as with others that are born bow-shaped, so that any vessel that nourishes one of the testicles does not bleed; for by this there is no harm, and if all the vessels come forth, it is necessary to draw out the testicles at all the vessels; so that the eyes do not lose their nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and dry up and are unable to help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the thread of silk
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, or l'estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l'un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, or de l'estension de li, and vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: or de percussion, or de saut, or de braire, or de levement de grief faix, and by semblants choses; and li signes quant c'est de l'estension dou syfac, si est qu'il avient poc et poc, in long time, and ne vient mie soudainnement; and est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l'intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the section of the silk, that it brings sudden pain at the beginning, and there are diverse appearances of abscesses beneath the skin close by, and this is because of the issue of the intestine and the body being torn away from the silk.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines descend with the intestine, and are retained in this way, and cause great pain to suffer from the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cases of iron cautery, there is fear, which is why it should be avoided.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	Et the manner of the work is that you instruct the patient to bring his intestine into his hand within the wound if he can enter it; then be placed on his throat between your hands, and lift the buttocks; then raise the skin above, and scrape off all the old skin from the length; then put inside the leeches of the size you need to open the wound so that the blood may issue forth; then cut off the fatty sac that is under the skin of the egg, as long as the white fatty sac remains uncovered on all sides; then place your two fingers in what guides the egg, between the white fatty sac which is under the skin of the womb and between the second fatty sac, and depart what is behind the womb, and between the second fatty sac; and then move your right hand inside the skin of the eggs, and place the white fatty sac above at your left hand, and lift the egg to the entire fatty sac towards the waist; and instruct the minister to stretch the egg upwards, and loosen what is behind the tie; and inquire if there is anything of the intestine wrapped or surrounded by the white fatty sac, and if you find anything, put it inside the belly below; then take a needle where it has ten threads, and put it in the back part of the fatty sac which is after the skin of the eggs; after the waist, then scrape off the hairs that appear from the threads, as long as there are four threads; then assemble one upon another in the manner of a cross, and tie the fatty sac with a strong cord of two parts; then wrap the hairs of the threads and tie them together with two parts, so that no servant who nourishes them can enter inside, lest an aposteme ensues; and place the tie above according to the first long tie one finger's breadth from that, and after these two ties leave the fatty sac which is under the skin of the eggs a finger's breadth wide; and then scrape in the part that is under the skin of the eggs as long as the blood flows, and be still, as we have said before; then apply moist linen to wounds, and put it inside, and apply the tie that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And at no time should you cauterize the white space that we have said, after the incision, due to fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Because it often happens, and leave the ligament until it yields to him; and if he tards in falling, thus be arisen with hot water, and put on what we have said, until it yields; then cure the wound with another remedy, until he is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case I never saw anyone who dared to do the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the old ones say that it is made like the thread that wraps around the arrow shaft, in such a way that you bind the vassals, after trimming them slightly above and below; then cut into the middle, and cure the abscess of those who work, until the vassals fall; and cure it as we have said, until he is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a routure comes in the groin area, as we have said, and opens up the abscess; and none of the intestines descend to the anus, and if any do, it is rare, and repair all hours; and yet, if he stays too long in this state, the wound or syphac grows, until the intestine descends; and this happens through the stretching of the syphac which is in the groin area, as we have said, for it is stretched, then softened and swelled the abscess and opens up; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes cured by iron in this manner: and is that the patient lies sovignly on his back between your hands, then cut the swelling of the routure from the wide according to the quantity of three fingers; and then extract the syphac which is under the skin that follows; then take the root and put it above the swelling of the syphac; and press at the bottom of the belly, then cut the two swellings of the syphac above the head of the root, and cut one and the other; then extract the head of the root, and do not cut the syphac nor stretch the contents or any other thing, as I have made known in the cure of the thread of the intestines; then cure by the cure of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you set the bones, so mend and care for the wound, until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The swelling is constrained, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cauterization is more effective in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the scrotum
