Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from lance or sword, and the wound is deep, then look to see if there are vents or effusions in the wound that the patient is complaining of: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not apply powder nor bind it for the blood that does not clot at the bottom, and revives at the heart, and kills the patient; but put on attractive ointment, and bind twice a day; and if you do not have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and make the patient sleep above the wound three days, or four, or more; then spasms will not come, nor evil tremors of heart nor strange movements; and when you see good dispositions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the then of tents and other cures, as long as it is cleansed; and if it cannot be cleansed, and work, then know that there is fistula; so cure it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a cut or thrust with a sword or knife, and it is simple, or worse on the back, then cure that which is in front; if it is large, by stitching; and if it is small, by powder, and if it is pressed into bone and there are splintered pieces, then cauterize the wound, and the hot irons if they are unwashed; and if they are not unwashed, let the wound suppurate, so that the extractions will ease; and for other wounds on other members, make judgments as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The disruptions of the belly are great and medium-sized and small; from a large wound sometimes an intestine or one of the intestines bursts forth, by which means the introduction of instruments is impeded; and suturing is more difficult, and sometimes the little wound is worth less than the big one, because when you put the intestines back in, they become inflamed as soon as they feel cold, so they go back in slowly, and for this reason the medium-sized wound is worth more, because you reposition the intestine to its place just like with other two And know that the rupture of the belly occurs in four ways: the two common sutures happen in the belly suture, and the sutures of other wounds of the body and two other proper sutures are common to other wounds; and although they are more proper with the belly suture, I will say each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	When the wound is small, and nothing from the intestines comes forth, and a great thing is to be put back, this is done by one of the two manners: or because the wound is small, as we have said, or because the intestine is inflated due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it thus: soak a sponge or cloth in lukewarm water only, or cook in hot water with cypress and spikenard, and apply the intestine until the swelling subsides; and sometimes make it stop again, and be careful that it does not become too full to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling departing, then moisten the intestine with water or hot and cold, as are cooked, for through this is eased the entrance to a small thing; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision with the instrument used to lance hemorrhoids; and the first care is to keep the wound closed, so that no one should cut without great necessity there being; and these are the instruments to split: then cut inside in the curvature and do not open it, and see where the shape is:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine jumps forth, then set it right again according to its natural form in its proper place, if you have the power, for this is necessary.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the part below the belly, then it is necessary that you make the patient lie on their back, and place their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the part below the belly, then place the head and chest higher than the parts below, and similarly if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, place your attention so that the injured part is higher than the other; and thus it is necessary to arrange what I say about large wounds and hernias.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	When the wounds are small, place what is necessary before you, then take a minister of pity who holds all the rupture in their hand and brings together the lips; and this is the common manner of stitching, and it is that you take one or more needles according to the quantity of the largeness of the wound, then leave a space of about an inch from the head of the wound and insert a needle where there is good strong thread; and pierce the two leather layers with the two leather layers underneath, which are below the leather inside, until you make it pierce on that side, and bring together the two heads of the siphac fourfold; then strain one double thread around the needle in two parts, then bring together the two lips of the wound properly, and then leave a space of about an inch, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did the first needle, and do not cease to do this with needles until the entire wound is restrained; and let the needles be moderate, between fine and thick, because fine needles cut through all the flesh, and too thick ones cannot well enter: therefore it must be that they are moderate; and do not insert needles too far into the flesh and leather, lest they cut and open the wound before the healing; then remove the needle heads so they do not bother the patient at night, and place tents or cloths on the needle heads to keep them from moving, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this manner of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because one or two needles are sufficient for the second stitching; and the second stitching is common, and it is that you bring together the two leather layers and the two siphac layers together on a needle where there is good strong thread moderate; and when you have pierced these layers all fourfold, then remove the needle from the part where you began, in the manner that one sews drapery; and leave a space of about an inch between each stitching; this stitching works for humans, and I stitched up a wound that one man had on his belly, who was wounded by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm long, and there were intestines two palms long inside, and the wound was in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine then when it had been there 24 hours full, and the wound was healed just to 15 days, and I cured it, and it was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the surgeon had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with oil, for I was in a place where one could not find any, nor any medicine; and I put cotton wool on top of the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing: take the needle and thrust it through from outside to inside as far as the core; when it has pierced the core directly in line, then tie off the siphac or thread where you put the needle, and make it pierce again on the other side of the inside part up to the outside; and the understanding of this suturing is that you sew just like the pelterers make pelts, and you leave once the siphac from one side and then take it back up the other, until the suturing is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of stitching, which Galen calls properly, is such that some make, who bring together the two parts naturally and apply one of the ends of the suture to the other end, in this way: drive a needle or point of the mirror close by, and let it pierce only that spot, and leave the two heads of the suture; then turn the needle and make it pierce from the outside part all the way through to the inside, at the two heads of the suture; then make both of them pierce from the outside part all the way through to the inside, in two other holes of the mirror that are on the other side; and this is the more tedious manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this saying, and some testify to it, so one should sew the belly with two needles, each having thread; and one should push in one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew corsets; and know that when there is a rupture in the belly, then the stitching is more difficult than for other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: and is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even as fire has changed it, so put back the intestine, and the skin; then put on powder enticing flesh, and if fire has changed it, put on some ointment that is present, until the wound closes; and clean the thread, and bind the stitches, and the bandages; then cure the wound as with others, until it is healed; and if you don't have medicine, then put on, soon as it begins to heal slowly, a cloth, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you don't need any other medicine in many cases where wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will not cause community with main members, it is necessary to anoint linen slightly with oil of temperate heat or oil of roses, and put it around the angles, and beneath the armpits; and if it feels pain or irritation in bowels, and often happens, then cleanse them with black wine vinegar, and similarly if the irritation reaches the intestine; and pierce within, knowing that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is injured, and this is because of the abundance of veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the entire body, and the approach to its nature from the kidneys.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the abscess jumps out of the wound, then put it back in its place just like the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned yellow or black, then you must tie up the part that is black, so that blood does not come forth, for there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ligament, and hang the two ends down from the lower part of the wound until the abscess falls out, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the belly
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people because I have seen a man injured by a lance blow to the stomach; and the wound was on the right side of the abdomen, and became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and excretion and flatulence were emerging from it; I applied treatment as I could, and did not cease to subtlety until he was healed, and the edges closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	Et when I saw him sewn, I doubted that the patient had an illness in his belly; and it was not so, but he remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and certain experimenters said that when one has a small wound in the intestine, he must be tied thus: take fresh figs to great testicles, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the figs have opened his mouth, place them above the two lips so that they strain his mouth up; and then cut off the head, and this holds so that it cannot come loose, and then put another fig after in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely covered; and close the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	That chief if it is sewn in the intestine, and there comes no harm to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a thin thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the head of this thread from the intestine that is very loose, and then tie it to the head of this thread with a subtle linen thread, then put the thread into the needle, and sew up the intestine, and wind it around; and this way of sewing with figs is no different than according to the path of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the great intestines, there is no reason or health, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or whatever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	All wounds or abscesses, when they turn septic, are universally called "fistula", and likewise when they burst open and flow downward.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the greenish nodulation, hard and white, where one does not feel pain, and it bursts forth like a bird's feather; sometimes clear and flowing downward, and at other times thick and dense; sometimes little, and at other times abundant; and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that all wound which is not healed, and there is no flesh, is nothing but due to one of the nine causes: namely, through smallness of blood or body; or because it is malicious; or because there is hard flesh within, and on the lips, that does not allow flesh to be formed; or because there is too much flowing; or the bone is rotten, and the material is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the treatment; or because corruption is a manner of pestilence; or because the property of the region is slow digestion, and tardiness in health, and is inclined by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and signs, and cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	And it is necessary that I let you know the treatment for fistula which is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistula occurs in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the great veins, and the arteries, and the nerves, or to the scrotum, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and so it comes to the property of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of grievous healing, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have said, and you have faith in the cure, and you recognize it, then take a tent of earth or iron, if the fistula is straight, then search for it; and if the fistula is twisted, then search with a subtle tent of cloth, because cloth bends around the twisting; and if the fistula has many pores and you cannot well search for it with tents, then flush it through one of the pores, because moisture flows from one pore to another, and cleans it; then let it bleed according to your power, as long as you know whether there is bone or nerve, and cut it off at a deep place, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and where he feels it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from jointure, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in some of the places I have said, then cut it according to what I have said, and remove the false humors and corrupted juices that are inside; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is well filled with right place, then you should cut off at a deep place, as long as you can, then put moist tents in medicine juice, and pour them just to the head of the fistula, as long as the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom; and then put ointments anointing sound flesh, until it is cleansed; and if it is not cleansed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then cut it off.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If vein or nerves do not bruise or principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, so let it be until all corruption is removed, then cure with things that belong to the charnel house until he is healed; and if he is not healed, and returns to its former state, know that you are not yet done: uncover and clear out everything until you reach the bottom, and remove all corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep to proceed; you cannot get there. If there's only one small bone corrupted and you can pull it with pincers, then pull it out with an instrument suitable for this purpose, and if there are many bones, then remove all of them, leaving none behind. And if moisture makes it contrary, and there's no mistake or fear, cut and dry and char the flesh and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	Et se tu ne les peux oster à une heure, si met sus la plaie chose enjaissant pourriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit pourri entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c'est uns grands os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noirur soit toute ostée, puis restoure la plaie; et s'il en i a grant partie du corrumput, et vient jusque à moitié de l'os; si le covient soier et couper tout jusque à la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu'il soit soudez; et je te dirai d'une fistule qui avint à un homme en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	It was about thirty young men who had a pain in their leg due to a cause that came from within the body, so much so that the materials came out into the leg and it became swollen with a big abscess, and there was no reason to open it; but the doctors through their foolishness worked on it for so long that the abscess opened, and many materials came out, and it turned into a fistula, and very bad pus came out that all flowed forth with moisture from the body; and many doctors treated it for about two years, and there was no skill in the art of healing until I was called to it, and I saw his leg and the medicines they were treating him with, and what was flowing through the fistula with great body; and the body of the young man became red, and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I tentatively pitched a tent in one of these cavities, and then searched all the cavities, and found that some were facing each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurried and probed one of the cavities until I uncovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and perforated, with corruption extending right into the bone inside; I saw what was appearing from the rotten bone, and thought there was no other corruption except that which I removed; and began to treat the wound with suitable medicines for a long time, but couldn't close it; then I recommenced, and uncovered the bone just as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and saw it, and then removed it, and was anxious to close the wound; but I didn't succeed until I probed around a palm's breadth from the bone, and pushed it all the way through, then restored it with medicines; and it became healthy and closed quickly, and there was no need to continue the treatment except for the patient's weakness, which couldn't tolerate it, and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because of the blood evacuation it often happened that he was often hemorrhaging, but he was fully cured, and instead of bone tissue a hard skin grew, and he was in good condition and had no harm or contradiction from anything at all, neither at rest nor on the move.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in some part of the body, then it must be treated in this way: take a thread, and strain it to the top of the exposed bone, and command someone to stretch it upwards; and place another linen thread, thicker than the first one, and tie it over the skin that is above the bone, so that you pull out the corrupted flesh below, and uncover the skin on the spot where you see fit, lest the bone touch the skin; and put a hot iron or a wooden splint under the bone to cover the corrupted flesh; and it is necessary to treat thus until one can see and feel the corruption, and treat again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	Et se li os est corrumpus, and n'apert mie, and li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, and puis soie des l'une partie a l'autre la corruption, and soit li soiure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, and soie l'os ou elle contient de l'autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n'i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corptions est ou poignil de la main, or ou poignil du piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t'apert; and la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu peux, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; and saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l'assise des os et l'apparence d'ous, and lor grossece et lor subtilite, and lor grandor et lor petitece, and lor duresce; and por ceu covient il appareillier a chescune semblance d'ovraige son estrument; and saiches que l'uevre te moustrera l'estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la connaissance de cest art, and le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l'estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu'il le covient.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; and when you have medicine that cures this corrosion by the cure of medicines, and it does not profit, then you must cover that member until the place where the corrosion comes, so that the patient escapes death or the evil that is greater than the failure of the member; and the signs are such that the member becomes black, as if it had been burned with fire, and afterwards it takes on a purple color, and then the corruption spreads from member to member, and takes hold throughout the body; if you hasten to cover, and this is due to the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as scorpion of the sea and viper and similar ones, if the corrosion is in the head of the vein, then you must cut it off, and not give it space to come to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, then cut at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, then cut at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no remedy except for the quantity of its virtue; and thus it is when the corruption comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, then cut after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, then cut the entire foot; and if it mounts to the leg, then cut at the knee joint; and if it comes from above the knee, there is no remedy except for the surgeon to kill the patient; and the manner of cutting or sewing the member is that you bind it above and below, and stretch one minister down and another up, and you remove the flesh between the two ligaments to a width of one spatium, until the bone is uncovered; then cut or sew, and put a linen wrap on each side, so that the seam does not touch the healthy place, and comes to the patient as other injury and swelling.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	Et si décorremens de sang vient quant tu oeuvres, si cauterise le lieu hastement, ou tu mets sus quelques poudres retenant; puis reviens à ta médecine tant qu'elle soit accomplie, puis lie le membre navré d'un lien convenable, et le cure tant qu'il soit saigné.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, and demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee of boughs; and then rots and pierces, and in so jumping the boughs, and remains the place void, as if vassals; and the skin that is above is as subtle as delicate drapes, and do not run just to bone, nor just to nerve, and such diseases are called "seam", and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so long that it comes just to the bone in the forefront, it is called "fistula"; and the skin is such that you cut off that skin all around, and similarly when it is subtle, as delicate drapes; and does not care for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have faith that the skin is healing, and the corruption is not in the forefront, and the skin is thickened with flesh, then cure it with a clyster of medicine thus: look to see if the nipples are large, and the bowels which issue forth are foul-smelling; then take equal parts of myrrh, oil, and lard, and put them in a vessel over fire, until the medicine is red and as thick as honey; and then take what you need according to your necessity, and make it into an infusion with water and honey, and use it to clean the womb and stop the perforation; and let the medicine stay for two hours before you express it; do this many times, until the nipples are cleared, and the foul odor is gone; and sometimes use a clyster of ashwater when this medicine is not present, and that is by taking ashes from vine wood, pouring water on top, then filtering it, and using it to clean, as long as you know the womb is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot endure the medicine or ashwater, then use a clyster of water and honey with a little litargire added; or use a clyster of honey and wine mixed, for the honey has properties to cleanse and wash, and the wine makes the skin breathe; and when you have done this, and you are sure that the womb is well cleansed, then use a clyster that causes flesh to grow in it, and that is by taking definitive emplaustre, and mixing it with rose oil and wine; or use some medicines and ointments whose properties I have described in the treatment of ointments; and if the perforation in the womb is small, and the clyster cannot enter, then enlarge it a little with a ferret, and put on an Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is enlarged; and if the wound is too large, then cover it and leave just enough room for the clyster to enter, and if the perforation that lets bowels pass is above, then cut or lower it so that it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Car when the bowels are in depth, do not let them linger; and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see, prepare it so that the bowels run to the lowest place there is; for when the bowels are in depth, do not let them linger and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see, prepare it thus: that the bowels run lightly downward and leave nothing of the bowels; and take consolidative medicines to put on the wound, and spread a cloth of linen that covers all the wound; then cut at the strongest point near the nipple where it is larger than before; then anoint with oil gently over another cloth according to the amount of the wound, and place it on the wound to relieve the bowels, and do not remove the large cloth until after many days once; and that which is on the wound, often removes to remove the bowels, and knows what comes out of the bowels, whether it be venom or pus or enough or digested or indigested; and beware if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in this manner and you see nature springing forth on the wound, know that the breasts are already set and approach health; then untie it in the morning or the third day, and when you open the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast discharges undigested pus after many days, know that the breast is not healed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons come after a long time, do not lose hope of health, for the healings approach.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men who take a long time to heal from their wounds, and those who do the opposite; and if undigested bile jumps forth from the chest after many days, know that the breasts are not sound; and if the breasts are slow to open up and are distant, mix medicines that are moist in substance and dry in virtue, as defined by ointment, for there is a great deal of vinegar, and this is the final medicine; take defined ointment and mix it with rose oil and equal parts of old wine; then cook and use it; and do the same for honey cakes when defined ointment is not present, or take myrrh, aloes, and incense, grind them, and powder them on honey when it is on the fire; then glue it to a cloth, and apply it to the breast, and sometimes administer aristologe longe, and celestial roots, which are also like flour of vetches and centaury; and use simple or composite remedies: grind them and make powder, and put it on the honey I mentioned, and use it; and if the treatment is prolonged, and is not cured by this treatment, then know that corruption has penetrated to the bone, and makes an impression on the bones, or in hard members, or in ligaments; so apply the cure of fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the tongue
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises under the nail of the finger or toe, or by chance in other places; and when it is neglected and one does not take care, then the abscess bursts, and flows and gushes so much that it runs to the root of the nail, and sometimes all the way through; and comes close to the bone, until a foul-smelling pain arises, and the joints of the toe are swollen, and the color is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit at all, then you must cut away all the excess flesh that remains from the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterization is very great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is sound; and if the nail presses against the flesh, and begins to prick and bleed, then it is necessary that you place a piece of lint under the nail that pricks the flesh, and put it on top, and cut away that subtle flesh carefully and lightly, and put above the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove all; then treat with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise. la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The knucklebones that are born in the hands of some men by chance are all cartilaginous, and by chance there may be a bone or a joint, and sometimes one is born at the root of the joint, where the birth is in some nails of the knuckle.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those that are born in the middle of the knucklebone do not move, and those that are born at the joint of the knucklebone, by chance, do move; the shape of the one that is cartilaginous is light, in the same way: it has its origin from a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those that are born at the root of the joint are difficult to cure: if you hold off from cutting.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one that is born or falls at the back knuckle, it is necessary that you cut away the cartilage around to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable thread for this, and then dress it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come together in the toes come from birth, or from a sudden wound, or from burning by fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you cut the seam, so that the knucklebone be repaired according to its natural forms; then put between two tents or moist cloths in rose oil, so it does not stick together; or you put between two thin pieces of cloth, until the wound is healed, as is fitting.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a swelling comes on any of his toes with the palm, then cut away that swelling in the same way as before.
des vils	of evils
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Wounds are large, swollen, and full of superfluous melancholy substances that come to many parts of the body; and it happens more often in the legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you administer to him at times an evacuation of bile, and then heal with the help of basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The iron treatment is done in two manners: one is to scrape and drain the black blood; and the other manner is that you lift up the vein and drain it entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is done in this manner: first, raise the leg with hot water very strongly until the thick blood is thinned, then strain the patient's leg from above the knee down to the part below the kneecap; then make an incision of a wide cut, either one, two, or three times, and lift up and drain entirely the black blood from one end to the other, as much as the patient can tolerate; and then bind it, and command that he eat meat until black bile is eliminated; and repeat the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, and it is harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: Raise the patient's leg if there is much hair, then put it in water and the arose leg in hot water until it becomes red, and inflate the veins; and if you do not have water, heat it by fire and then apply it to the vein at the long bone of the knee or below it near the ankle; then smooth out the skin to the onciné, and scrape off the vein from each part until it appears when one feels it; and it is seen red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord; then put the weight underneath, until it is lifted from the skin, and then lift it to the onciné lightly, then apply it in another place three times; then scrape off the skin above the vein until it appears, then lift it to the weight as you have done, and lift it to another onciné as you have done first; then apply another size or more if necessary, then lift it, and apply it to the toe of the foot, then train and lift just to the second size; then lead it from size to size, until it is all free, then apply it; and if you cannot lead and lift it, put a needle in every strong thread double, and lift and lead it, and put it underneath the weight, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until there is some; and be sure it does not apply, for if it applies, you cannot lead or lift it, and it will harm the patient; and when you have led it all, put a damp cloth on the site of the wound in vinegar and rose oil; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it's not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it awry, but don't cover it up; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron that one uses to open the vein is curved, and does not cut through, so it opens the vein; and it's thick, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but let it be as we have said, and this is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is situated in the legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and on land where there is no moisture; and by chance it may arise elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to the corruption that comes from beneath the skin, as it comes from inside the body like serpents and worms, situated between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there is a very great inflammation in the leg, then it changes its hue, and the vein begins to come out, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the wound opens, it is necessary that you wrap a piece of linen around it from one and a half to two inches, and tie it off, and leave the linen on the leg, and every time it needs to be reapplied at the far end, wrap it around the linen again; and if it is too long, cut off part of it, wrap the remaining portion, and do not cut it in its root, until it is completely out; for if you cut it, it will return to the flesh, and cause an abscess and putrefaction at the site, and a bad disease; therefore it is necessary that it be treated gradually up to the head, and leave nothing behind in the body; and sometimes this vein when it is treated, reaches five or ten inches long, and one man came to me whose it was ten inches long, and when you cut it, it bursts forth like a spring or a perforation, and all comes out; and the material inside should be empty, and medicinal treatment should be administered to prevent putrefaction any day, then the cure is as for abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And at times there are many purges, and indeed when it opens in the ankle joint or foot, or foot and ankle, and it comes out with much pus, and then there is purging; treat it thus as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	boils that arise between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "bovine sickness", because it often afflicts oxen, and it is a small boil that arises between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body ascending and descending, and one can feel it as it moves from member to member, until it bursts open where it was going and jumps away; and it is caused by some sort of humor, such as worms, serpents, lice, or tape worms in the belly; and one doubts its maliciousness, for when it goes through the body, and it reaches the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance it returns, and destroys the eye; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it cured and pulled, one cannot delay except when it goes: then it is necessary that you tie the top and bottom with a strong rope tightly, then strike up and pull out the root, and if the vein runs deep into the flesh and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire above, until it turns; and the greatest harm it causes is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the head close to the eye, then press below it the ring tightly, then strike up, and pull out the root; and it is necessary to use the patient with a cleansing of the body with soluble medicines for bad humors, and beware of unwholesome foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From the pain that comes from windy affliction
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some members, and it can move from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was summoned to a sick woman, and she revealed her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and afterwards, I saw it rise also like a worm on the shoulder, more quickly than any thing, just as vivid silver when it runs from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and settled in the shoulder, and then a little afterwards coursed through the entire body, so far as she came into the other arm; then she told me that she was turning around the body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how she moved from member to member in this way, for I had never seen this disease move like that before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had thought that many people wanted to move the pain from one place to another, but I did not think so, as I saw in the woman; and I thought it was because the woman's body was dry, and her veins were uncovered, and therefore this phenomenon appeared constrained; and they did not notice according to this reason those who are lubricated, and have moist bodies and responsive veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to healing this sickness, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens up as we have said, then bind it above and below quickly, and then cut on top until those ventosities are constrained to go away; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it at your hands, then treat with those who counteract ventosities, such as fetid pills, and serpentine pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the parts of the body where they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of their kinds is that there are those which have large points, small, and hair-like, and soldered; and those which have two angles, and those which have tongues, and those with pieces; and that one which falls in any member falls in two ways: or it falls in the principal member as cerveil, heart, liver, peritonium, reins, intestine, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, appears to you: so it is necessary that you beware of the extraction of this arrow, for many die afterwards in various dispositions; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then take it out and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain is when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and the skull bursts forth which is above the brain; it shows scotoma and sodality and eversion and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of tongue, and spasms and mixing up of understanding, and vomiting of gall; and perhaps it is without sense from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps it hinders speech and voice; and there is a white moist wound similar to pustules, and also like a charred log; and if this sign appears, you should take care and remove the arrow if it's not too deep.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it hits or pierces the heart are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; and by chance the arrow moves just like the hair, and in cold black blood, and comes with chilliness and cold sweat, and faintness: know then without doubt that death ensues.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.
