And the sign of the arrow that pierces the womb is when without foam it jumps out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face turns color, and he sighs high and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow pierces the covering of the breast, then it is below the small ribs; and it yields a great deal of pain and great anguish and sighing; and all the members of the shoulders are moved.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow pierces the stomach, perhaps something from undigested food jumps out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow pierces the belly, and in jumping it does not pass through the large intestine, then there is no hope for the cure or the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow pierces the bladder, and urine jumps out and comes forth, and the patient feels very great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulders, and loins of the back, and the ribs, and hips, and legs, and similar members are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you, because I experienced it thus, so that you may do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	An arrow struck the house of the brain in the root of the nose: I pulled it out and drew it to the other side under the fatty layer of the ear, and he was healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I drew out an arrow that had struck the fat under the eyebrow, and the arrow was stuck, and I could not grasp it except for the tip of it, and the arrow was as long as a Turkish bow, to all appearance without any harm; the joint was healed, and no evil accident came to it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And pull out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabian with ears; I plucked out the feathers, and refined it until I pulled it out, and the Christian became well.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And pull out an arrow from the man, that was stuck in his belly, and thought he would die; and then after passing thirty days, his condition did not change; I cut above the arrowhead, and signified it, and pulled it out, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if the arrow falls on a man's back, and the wound is sewn up above; and the arrowhead remains inside him, and does not change his natural disposition, nor finds harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see another man, to whom an arrow fell on his face, and the wound was sewn up; and it remained thus without suffering great pain; and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And draw out an arrow from the home of the prince's king, which had stuck in his neck, and was slightly declining to the right side; and the arrow was entirely embedded. I was summoned for treatment after it had been stuck for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I searched it with all a subtle tent, and did not feel it; and he felt pricking and pain below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow I put on the wound a plaster attracting and digestive, because the flesh did not swell; and the flesh of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the plaster on for many days, and the wound closed up again, and the patient remained thus for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his neck; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied corrosive medicine to the wound by hand for many days, until it was open, and I tried it, and felt the tip of the arrowhead which had settled at the base; then I probed the opening of the wound with that medicine until the arrowhead appeared visibly; and it went well beyond IIII months, and then it healed so that I put in forceps, and pried open one side and the other, and could not come out; then I did not cease to subtlety and ingeniously devise methods with instruments, until I got the forceps well made on the first day, according to what its shape would be at the end of this chapter, as long as I pursued it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctor judged that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored; I restored it then, and the wound was closed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or that is said the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your cure on what I do not say, for books cannot grasp all; but wise masters know well a little thing, and about what is present and lacking, they provide nine times work, and nine instruments, at the understanding of strange things which happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come from the members where they are fixed except by two manners: or through the way in which they enter, or from another part; and that which jumps forth on the other side of where it enters is an arrow entering the flesh, and sometimes jumping forth again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it doesn't jump forth now, then leave it until the flesh is thoroughly pierced around and the issue is eased; and similarly if it's fixed in the bone and can't come out, then leave it like that for some days, and gently move it each day; and then it will jump forth, and if not, then pierce all around with a very fine point, until the flesh around is stretched out, and then treat it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	Et if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the skull and goes just up to one of the vents of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said occur to the patient: then do not pull it out, but let it stay as long as it is even for a few days, because if the arrow comes just short of the sacrum, it's death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not come up to the sacrum, and the patient remains for a few days without bad accident, then he should be encouraged to remove it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very stuck and cannot come out further, then I administer tarers around, as I have said to you; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged in the flesh of the body and cannot be seen, then seek to extract it from all the tent. And if you can feel it, then pull it out with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound or the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then cut away enough flesh to make the wound larger; and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears that hold it in place, then remove the flesh that is stuck to it by two parts as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow until you can pull it out; and be subtle so that you do not break the arrow, but rather pull it out more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, then leave it until the skin around is ripe, and then pull it out, for the extraction will be freed.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	Et if the bleeding makes you contrary, so manage what we have said about cure in this chapter; and beware of incising the nerve and vein, and consider how you can draw out the arrow without danger, soon or late, firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form he was when the arrow hit him, for that is the greatest aid there is, and if you cannot, then put him according to what the sign shows.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, if it appears to be attached to something or the skin is swollen in that place and can be seen or felt awkwardly: cut then above, until the forceps can grasp it, and then pull it out; if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then turn your hand around gently, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, so leave it and then resume the extraction until it comes out; and if the arrow head is stuck, so wrap it with all the wrappings; and if the arrow head falls, and you see fit to administer poultice, so administer one instrument, hair-covered, so that the point of the arrow goes into the fur of the instrument; and then push forward, and if the arrow is removed, so wrap the instrument with the point entering in, in order to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is stuck, then it is necessary that you cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, and then treat the wound as it should be treated.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow hits or falls on the head, belly, bladder, or ribs, and it is close to, and you can cut into it, then cut into it; and beware of cutting the vein and the nerve, and then pull it out, and then treat the wound as necessary; and cure it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The forms of tweezers used to remove arrows are similar to a bird's beak, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many forms: large, small, and medium-sized, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is like the feathers of a bird, in order to push against the point of the arrow, as it is shaped:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of tweezers to push and to grasp if it is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	The veins that one uses to bleed oneself are thirty-one, of which there are sixteen on the head, to wit: two jugulars that are after the ears, which are called "herbech"; and the two temporal arteries that are in two temples appearing; and two veins that are in two corners of the eyes, which are called "aspires"; and one vein that is in the forehead; and one vein that is at the crown of the head; and the two nape-veins that are in the neck; and the two labial veins above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins commonly used for bleeding are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, located on the left side, and people call it "the vein of the head"; and the median is called "fast" and is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and people call it "the vein of the heart"; and the basilic is located on the right side, and people call it "the vein of the belly", and it is above the clavicle, and that is the one used for bleeding, which opens clearly above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saphenous vein is the one that is between the wrist and ankle veins, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is below the pocket of the left side, and the second saphenous vein is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein called "nesse" which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: and is that the patient strains his neck, so much so that the two veins appear clearly; and feels the pulse below his throat, then signs off; then lifts the key above the vein at his index finger's height, inserts the lancet below, lifts the vein up, cuts it, just as you did with two other veins, and does what is necessary with the blood according to your need; then frees the patient, and places your hand on the vein for an hour, then covers it with cotton; then binds it tightly, and leaves it until it heals; and we have spoken of their binding and extraction, or the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The vein of the forehead is as valuable as the cephalic vein in treating old face diseases, and migraines, and headaches; and the quality is that the patient strains his neck by twisting, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and strike with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity you see; then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is well-bleeding and at times make a wide incision.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not good that the inflammation be too great; and the wound will cross over, for the bone is close, and by chance break through when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood of the two veins that are in the eyelids helps those with ulcers, and pimples, and headaches, and cataracts in the eye, and face diseases; and the quality of their blood is that the patient strains his neck by twisting without any connection, just as before; then let it bleed, and be the bleeding of the traverse, a little bit long, a little bit wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the inflammation is subtle, it may break through; then make the wound bleed, as much as you need, and then bind with cotton, and bind well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bleeding from the neck vein is very valuable for the treatment of ague, and for fever without delirium, and for facial diseases, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, and especially when it is old; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient will tighten their neck, then strain their nose towards their left hand, and take a subtle flame long, and place it between the two nostrils in the space that is between them, for the vein does not open well there, and the blood will start flowing now; do not go too far into the depth, and make the bleeding flow according to your necessity, then let it rest for a night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the bleeding:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bleeding from the two jugular veins helps with the constriction of the arteries, and the beginning of inflammation, and many diseases, and epilepsy, and corrosion, and herpes, and edema; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient tightens their neck above and below, as we have said; and let the master be standing on the head of the patient, and the patient sit in a siege, then bleed the long vein slightly wider, then draw out the blood temperately, or as much as is needed; then do the other side in the other vein, then release the tie, and tighten the veins moderately so that the patient does not choke; and leave it until morning, when the wound will be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the wounds
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The juice of the veins from the leaves above helps to heal in the mouth, and to corrupt gums, and splits in lips, and around the nose.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the health are to make the patient sit before you, and hold his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right side of the lip and the other on the left, and know them by this that they are black, and by this that there are small black lines around them: cut then both and if you do not recognize them and you are in doubt, then cut the larger one from each side, and do the same with the two veins above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the health below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The health of the veins that are below the tongue so helps after the cephalic health, and it is for the constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of the one who practices this health are that the patient will sit between your hands in front of the sun, and lift up his tongue, and look below on each side a black vein: heal then both and do not go too deeply, because there are arteries underneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	Veins of the scalp which are commonly cured are healed in two ways: or they are punctured by a wide and strong mirtin, or olive oil so fine as to cut through, and is called "anesil"; and are wide and fine according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flannel is very well known, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the scalp veins that are full of thick blood appearing, and which contain thick blood and turmoil; and this is the form of olive oil.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtly pointed, and it is for bleeding thin veins, where there is subtle yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are below the throat, and under the neck, and under the chest; and it is necessary for the healer to let blood, and be cautious of the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if the artery is cut and bleeding blood comes forth, then it is necessary to stop the bleeding, as I have said; and one should not pierce with the olive oil, but rather cut through as with anasyl.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, then you should extract it, and change another one; or you want some kind of thing from it, or you let the vein open in its place in the arm: it opens manifestly; and cut with the fire antiseptic, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to know the location of the vein, then it is necessary also that you extract the arm, and touch the location until you know the pulse; then sign the location with ink, and bind the arm, and open the vein with the fire antiseptic; and beware that you do not strike in the artery when you see the location swollen, for it is of the artery: cut away then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it come out above like a child's urine, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is blood from the artery: hurry then, and place your finger on top for a long time, then remove your finger if the bleeding subsides, which often happens; bind the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient; and be careful, and do not move until they are healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped, and it flows forth, and medical supplies are not present, then cut the artery if it opens, for the head of it retreats; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a rind of fistic, and cut it, and take one half and tie it well just to the other day; if the wound stays open, that's good; if not, then treat it with the powders that stop blood; and the stopping is not at all grievous in many dispositions due to the smallness of the wound, and the strength of the ligament of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein of the vein is in the medium so that it treats blood from the top of the head and from beneath, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic, as we have said; and it is necessary for the surgeon to beware of the nerve which is below, and if he pierces too deeply and finds the nerve, and it swells up and the wound becomes grievous, and by chance cannot heal; and this nerve shows itself many times, and if it does not show itself in some men due to its subtlety, then you must let the veins of the instrument anesthetize; and avoid wounding the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, then cut it longwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The wound of the cephalic vein helps, which draws blood from the head and aids the eyes; and it is necessary to bleed in a painful spot using olive oil or myrrh oil, because this is the most saving of all veins, since there is no nerve nor artery underneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to seek the lighter seat, and not cause any harm if you fail the first time, and then start again; and by chance some people's joints swell, when you fail the first time, but do no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is not done except to preserve health and to ward off diseases that are to come; and the bleeding should be done in one of the three veins that are there: namely, cephalic, facial, and basilic; and one should bleed at the beginning of Lent, and in autumn and winter after meals, when the sign of repletion appears; and one should bleed on the first or third day after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The sick person who is ministered to for illnesses has no fixed hour determined, but only when need arises by day or night, at all hours and in all times; and it is not necessary to heal children until they are 14 years old, nor a woman carrying more than four months pregnant until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should one bleed those who are very old and have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be healed, in whatever way it may be, it is necessary that they purge their intestines with a light clyster if they have many filthy substances retained, so that the veins do not attract the superfluous and harmful matters from the intestines to the principal members; nor does one heal who is too fatigued by food, or drunk, until they are cured; nor those who are dropsical; and beware of healing after a passion of colic, vomiting, and flatulence, and frequent urination, and labor, watching, and fasting, and all that can harm the virtue, either by something from outside or inside the body; then refine the humors if the blood is thick, with food, drinks, and medicines, as you have the power; then bathe in a bath, unless something prevents it, to refine the blood, and heal the swelling around the breast after the third hour, as we said; and be careful that day of labor, and of paining, and of lust, and similar things; and be merry and joyful, and let the healer be higher than he who is being healed, and stroke the arm two or three times, then loosen the ligament in moderation, for if it is too tight or too loose, the blood cannot flow; and then wet the healer's hand with a small amount of old oil, then place their left hand on that swelling under the breast a little below where they want to be healed, so that the swelling does not become inflamed.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Car it has veins that flow like strings to the surgeon, and if there are those that are full of windy-ness, so that when one puts on the flame, it retracts from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of these; and if he opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, therefore it is necessary for the surgeons to be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens at the first attempt, that is good; if not, then one recommences a little below or above that place in haste, if the limb is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the swelling is increased, and the patient becomes frightened, let him rest for one or two days, and do not bind the arm: lest an abscess forms suddenly; do not enter the bath, then resume the treatment if he wishes it; and if the opening is small, or the wound is subtle and you doubt that it will not bleed as much as you see, be confident in that same opening for all the flame directly; and work a little hastening, while the swelling is increased; for this has often happened when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the swelling inflamed, do not re-start the wound dressing, and put on a bit of oil's leukorrhea, because it lightens the body of blood, and is moistening in this place the leukorrhea that the oil; and thus administer the oil's leukorrhea to each wound that you dress the veins, in order to stop the flow of blood; and the same thing does triad and bowels too, when one puts it on the swelling; so subtly the sinews and part when it is too big.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a big abscess comes, which often happens, especially when it is not fully healed or the opening of the vein is small, then hurry, and put a moist sponge on the swelling in water and a little hot seal, and squeeze it for an hour; and you must do this after the blood has stopped flowing from the vein, and if it remains at the swelling after some days with any blackness or greenness, it will not harm him; and if you see, put something of aloes or myrrh dissolved in camphor, musk, or similar thing.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there appears an abscess and swelling at the basilic vein: then put your hand on it, and if you find the limb soft to the pressure of the hand, that is the bad swelling.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not put anything of what we have said on it, for by chance there may be a lack of blood from the artery; but make one application of dry poultice to harden the limb, then treat with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each blood according to its quantity and virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it is thick, let it become thinned out; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for the one who is weak and feeble, and has need of bloodletting, to make a larger incision and have wide flaps; and for the one who is frail, do the opposite, and let him recover quickly and often, and he must be healed by cutting across, not piercing; and this manner of healing is preserved from corruption of blood and numbness of nerve, and is worth more than the healing of length or width.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to the one whose body needs healing, it is necessary to give moist bread soaked in apple pears; if he is overheated, then treat with bloodletting three times or four. And if he has a cold complexion, then anoint his bread with sweet syrup before healing, or with aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and saffron, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it palms to the vein, after a great deal of blood has issued, then it is necessary that he drinks broth of flesh and aromatic subtle syrup, and uses other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to vent his arm and heal another time, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bloodletting, that he heals little by little, according to the quantity of his virtue, continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to vent his arm after the first bloodletting, and he has strong body, then he heals in 7 hours after the first bloodletting, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if one wants to heal from another part, then he should heal on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Because there is much blood inside the body that is already overheated, and it causes fever; then it is necessary to draw out a great quantity, and widen the vein so that it can be opened easily; after which you reward all the conditions of the wound, and place your hand on the pulse when it is healing, lest death come in the place of paining, and this often happens when the surgeon is neglectful; and it does not matter at all when you see the arm untied, and blood issuing for the second time, and the vein is closed, that you press strongly down; nor if it is curved, that it stretches out the arm quickly, for that would be bad; but let it stay until it heals the second time; or you point to the tip of the flame, until the frozen blood which has congealed at the wound issues forth, and place a poultice on top, remade in water, and press down lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is inflamed, then let it be and do not bind it tightly, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires drawing blood the second time, then let it be done in that same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein within the arm is healed in place of the jugular vein because it is compounded.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of healing is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the boil is red; then it is tied moderately so that the vein appears well, and the healing takes place through the middle, not the width or length; and the pores are large, and the healing is close to the joint of the hand, and if there is no issue, one puts the hand in hot water again, and lets the blood run into the water until you have enough; and if it is in winter, one should not put the hand back in hot water, for it is more harmful than helpful; and the healing of this wound is safer than all other wounds, since there is no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The healing of the saved part of the right hand is worth more than all diseases of the liver, and this is how to do it: strain the hand and put it in hot water until the vein is emptied, so that one can see; and if the wound heals from the side, and you cover it entirely, then it will not cause any harm; and don't go too deep beneath the surface, for the nerves are hidden under all the flesh, and then put the hand back in hot water if the blood congeals in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let blood as much as is necessary, then put oil and silk on the vein to close it quickly, and thus do for each one.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The healing of the vein on the left hand is worth more for the illness of the mouse, and do all the same as I have told you regarding the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The wound of the sophene is worth all the diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the stomach, and retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and of the hips and ancient legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its wound is that the patient must put their foot in hot water, and rub on the vein as long as it flows, and tie above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many rains; then it will heal either a wider rain or at the ankle, which is worth more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, then beware of the nerves that are underneath, and let the healing be across as in cutting; and let the flaps be evenly stitched.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water and let it drain well from the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the wound does not heal at first, it will recommence on the second attempt above a little, for the bone is salty; do not doubt the nerves, as we have said, and thus make the same treatment of the sophene on the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The flesh of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of force, and its healing is worth for the pain in the back, when it's due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	Et the qualities of his blood are such that the patient goes into the bath, and stretches above the ankle 4 times in twisting, for otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, then heal him in all ways you can, and crossing over; and value it more that you cover it, for the limb is sound, and it is very responsive to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you don't bind it, then heal any part of the blood that opens on the back of the foot and towards the little toe, and beware of nails; and do so much good with the blood as you see, and then untie the bandage, and put cotton on and strain it; now it is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	woundings of cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping-glasses are made of horns, or of iron, or of glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by piercing and attracting blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is without piercing is done in two ways: either it is done with all fire or without fire; and the cupping that is done by piercing and extracting blood is done on 14 parts of the body, some of which are on the head; others in the neck; and 2 on each side of the neck; and one under the chin; and one on each shoulder; and one on the hips; and ones on both arms; and ones on both legs; and ones on both ankles. And cupping does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it is not weakened much, just as with a wound treatment; and it should not be administered, neither at all fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even more so when it is in the middle of the month, we command them to cup after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The sainie of the muze so helps to the grieving of the head that comes to the eyes and does not need to be after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventosation is in lieu of the sainie of the cephalic, and does not need to be used by those who are of cold complexion or have a catharrh, for it would do them great harm; and therefore it is not necessary that those with hot rashes or who have cold diseases use it.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who cure themselves often, become forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to put the cupping-glass a little lower down due to the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventosation into the neck is in lieu of the sainie of the head and the basilic, and for this it is worth it for the constriction of the belly, and the splitting of the channel of the peritoneum, and for all, and for repletion; and it should not be pressed too hard, because if it holds too firmly, it will injure the obliance or stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, and obtalmie et emigrainne, and to the strangulation, and to the pain of the roots of the teeth, and is in the place of the salvation of the basilica; and it is necessary that you command the savior that he spread his hand when placing, so that he does not cut the artery, and there be no flowing of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The cuppings below the chin are worth for mouth diseases, and for corruption of the gums, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is in place of the bleedings from both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The cuppings on the shoulders are worth for the disease that comes from heat and repletion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, for it takes blood from these large veins; and command the savior not to cut too deeply, for the place is bare of flesh, and there are nerves and arteries underneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping-glass that is on the hip is worth for hemorrhoids of the fundament, and for diseases below, and it is necessary that the cupping-glass be large, and made of iron, so that it can draw well; and by chance, if they were small, they would break; and this makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cuppings on the legs are said to heal obviously, for they draw blood from all the body, and are worth for old pains in the kidneys, bladder, and womb, and restore the flowers; and they take the place of the two Sophene bones and the two ankles, and although they weaken the body after long use, they bring on fainting in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the cupping-glass is that you first empty it, and then apply it with a gentle touch, and place it hastily, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the red and swollen area, and observe the flow of blood; then pierce, and remove the cupping-glasses, and take heed of the condition of the body, for there are those who have thick skin, and clear pores: so it is necessary to strike once only, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and slightly deep ones; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to draw out the blood little by little, we should only do it once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want much blood, so we repeat often; and if the blood is thick, so cut deep, and the ends will be perceived suddenly, and it is necessary for those who have tough skin and hard, and who have large pores, that you anoint the places of the cupping glass with an oil that is aperitif and dissolvent: if it's in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it's in winter, with wormwood oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	and if the excesses are big and cold, take bitter oil, or balsamite oil, or wormseed oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person to whom one gives medicine has a tender skin and large pores, there is no need to put oil on it, but rather wash it after the ventilation with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And the one who has too much moisture, should rise up with ease, or with water of myrtle, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large superfluities should lift up old wine, or water of sedge, or decoction of anise or camomile, or similar things; and one does not need to heal with a poultice before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and one should not sleep after the ventilation, and it is necessary that he warn himself when he should be ventilated and when he is ventilated.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware of those who are sick and are choleric, and their sweat is too abundant and inflamed; then it is necessary that he take cold things, such as quinces, endives, and lettuce at ease, and similar things; and eat pomegranates, and the flesh of a rooster, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, take a syrup of honey and aromatic wine, which is between old and new, and eat little meat, and few small birds and pigeons; and the day when he will sweat, he should drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men a tryptic or muscat before ventosation, or after, to comfort the main members; and let the blood flow slowly, but it does not need that those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The poultices that are applied without causing harm are those that are applied on the liver, and on the kidneys, and gout, and on the belly and the backside and the hips and the haunches, because those members do not endure being struck or hit on those places; and it is done only to draw blood from member to member, just as we apply poultices on the breasts when the milk flows; in order to remove the viscosity that is in the member, just as we apply poultices on the belly and backside to reduce the member; and removes the pain when there is inflammation or swelling; and it so happens by its attracting power that it draws out the inflammation, or reduces the swelling from its place; and thus it does when applied on the liver and kidneys when there is retained moisture; and these poultices are administered empty only to suck up as much as possible; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes plain water, just like in diseases of the eyes, and in such a way one fills the poultice with warm or hot water.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the poultice administered to fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont,
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should thus put this poultice on the member: take a candle of wax or linen, and place it inside the poultice in the middle of the handle which is inside the poultice, so that the wick be at the bottom of the poultice that it does not burn the patient; and then place it on the member, and it should be above the perforation which we have said, so that when you want, the vapor goes out, and remove the poultice; and reapply the poultice as before, and repeat often if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the poultice then which is administered in illness of pleurisy, always wet, has no handle nor perforation, and is only administered when it is full of water, and is placed on the member solely; and that's the form.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Poultices are only applied when needed in members where it is not possible to put poultices due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar parts; and in bare bones, such as toes or nails, and others similar; and the quality of the user is that when you find poultices that are in sweet, clean water without any impurity, then take them; and put one into a sweet water bath until they become familiar, and have nothing in their bellies; and then let them be sutured with wine and poultice, then rub the member until it is red, and put on the poultices; and when they are full and bursting, if it is a place where one can put a poultice, then apply it, for this is very valuable afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then lift the limb gently, and then in water, very well, and then squeeze it; and if the swelling increases too much after the wound, then soak a linen cloth in cold water, and apply it so that the swelling subsides; and if the swelling is excessive, then apply vitriol powder or galenas, and similar things, until it subsides; or you may put half of cooked peas on the limb, and leave them until they stick to the limb, then it will subside now; and if you need more, take other remedies.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the remedies do not take hold, then rub the limb with fresh blood, or insert a needle until the swelling goes down, and then apply them, and soon as they feel the blood, they will stick; and when you see that they are falling away, then powder on some alum and silk dust, or ash, so they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here is the translation:
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is a remedy for breaking and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Dear son, know that foolish men see nothing of this chapter, for they have never seen a single ancient book or letter; and because of this reason the science is strange in our land, for I found no good; and I know nothing, except through the science of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science and by experiment and by habit of my life; and I have described what is contained in this chapter and abridged it at the end and clearly shown the forms of instruments used, just as I did in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.
