And if there are some of the toes broken, restore them, as we have said about the fingers; then put a splint on each broken toe according to its length, and make it a little wider; then put that plate under the foot that I mentioned, and bind it accordingly; and if there are two or three or more broken, put a splint on each toe according to its quantity, wrapped in one piece of linen, and bind the plate under the foot; and let it be so that the top of the plate is outside the foot, so that it holds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things I have said about other breaks, as we have said; and treat each accident as it requires.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the breaking of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	When the bone of the thumb of man is broken, or that of woman, then restore it thus as we have said in the bone of the hanch; and these fractures are not hidden from him who puts his study and use there, and heeds my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture signifies in many ways the right path of restoration: heed this therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's gizzard and pour it into the penis; then wrap cloth around it, and leave it for three days or so, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for someone who has a break with a wound, whether it be great like the bones of the hip or shoulder or similar, to be healed now, so that the wounds we have said bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then wash it with vinegar, if you have nothing else, and then continue to restore the break in the same hour or day, unless there is an abscess that comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess comes, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, so that the abscess is pacified, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would bring a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent above the knee uncovered, it is necessary that you set it in place slightly with your hands, to a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not ready to be put in place by your hands, then use this instrument which is of iron, which has seven or eight fingers or length, and its width is according to the quantity of the wound; and it is necessary for the doctor to take three or four, depending on what he needs for each cure of a break; and be straight and a little thick, so that it does not bend at all under compression on the member in your work, and be curved forward, and thick from the middle going forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", for which it is necessary that the curved nail be placed on top of the apparent bone; and bind it once, until it recovers, and let them be equal one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the instruments cannot well take hold of the bone, then it is necessary that you cut off the top of the bone, until the instruments have power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone as we have said, then cut it off with an instrument suitable for this purpose, or a saw or file, to your ability; then take out what remains in the bone of roughness and small scales.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	So it is in its place, then soak the cloth in black stiptic wine and apply it properly; and do not put a poultice or anything else on the wound where there is oil, lest you bring forth rot and corruption; then administer remedies when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover all around with wrapping, according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not constricted with the breakage; and many times this has been done by foolish surgeons, and they have brought forth on the patient death or corruption sometimes; and the constriction be softer and gentler than other breakages.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is foul or large, and you doubt that bad accidents may come to pass, as we have said, and you find pain at the joint, then it is not necessary to put remedies on; but wrap hard cloths around, instead of remedies, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two the boweling of the wound, then take away all that you have put on top to drink wine, and put a balm good for wounds, as a balm four-drug and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the member twice a day, morning and evening, until it is set and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the members be arranged in such a way that the bow runs down lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it happens to happen many days, and it cannot heal but the bow returns, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which it is necessary that you search the wound with a tent, and remove all these uneven pieces that bring about that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or another manner of corruption, then it is necessary that you cure it, according to what is said in this chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken, and appears on the limb, such as the hip or shoulder bone, and similar ones of the great limbs, then do not pull it away, for many times death ensues, but leave it until it can heal; by chance it may fall out after twenty days or thirty, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of blisters that come on the swelling
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often see after the healing of the swelling, namely when it is near the jointure, and it is a bad thing to see the figure of the member; and by chance the members cannot perform their natural works.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take heed therefore if the wound is fresh: administer stiptic medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acaica, and similar others, either taking one of these things or all together, and mixing them with stiptic wine or with abundant egg white or with oil; and apply it to the joint at night in an estoup, and press it well, and do not remove it for several days; then remove it, and begin another, until the swellings are removed; or you strain it on a piece of linen well made; for the properties of linen are such that they remove all swelling from the members; and if the swelling has already been converted into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut above, and make the superfluity apparent; or give it to any barber, until it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after the healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the breaking of the bone is restored, and remains after the member weak and subtle, this happens for many reasons: one reason being that it was tied too tightly, and not as it should have been; or because there were too many ties, and could not come the nourishment to the member; or due to excessive inflammation; or due to great movements, but not in its hour; or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat and cause their body to become tender, until the blood is multiplied in them; and administer baths, and give them joy and relaxation; then apply poultice on the member, so that the poultice attracts great nourishment, and inflammation often subsides with lukewarm water, until nourishment flows into the member; and returns to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the twisted member after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is twisted after restoration, and the broken bone appears, and the shape of the member is ugly, though it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish who say that one must break the member all over again; many foolish physicians have done this in our land; and this work is blameworthy, and great evils come from it, and by chance death ensues; however, if the swellings and tortures are fresh, then it is necessary to rise them with hot water, or cooking soft herbs such as those of mallow, and roots, and melilotus, and similar things; and make a soothing plaster, such as one made from dyaquilon well prepared, and take the mucilage of mallow, and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top; or take fat figs, and grind them with rye flour, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the swelling is cut off because of continuous and long friction with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be gentle movement to the member each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is hardened and toughened, like stone, and it is necessary to remove it with iron, then it is necessary to cut just to the bone, with a subtle and light incision; and apply caution and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to someone, then it is necessary now to bring them back gently.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the swelling increases, and by chance if it is reset with points at the swelling; therefore it is not fitting to move it until it has deflated: many times it brings forth shame and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, make the patient well, then leave him, until the abscess has been pacified; then arise the member in warm water and oil, then gently reset it, and cure each member as the treatment comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters of dislocations from top to toe.
des mandibules	of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It often happens that the jawbones are dislocated and downwards, and the dislocations of both sides occur in two manners: either they are slightly removed from their places, and somewhat softened; or they are entirely dislocated, and hang down towards the chest, and cut off the saliva of the mouth so that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and involuntarily wrap his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by gentle means.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, then it is fitting to reset it quickly, and do not delay; and in this manner, the minister holds the head of the patient, and places the mirror's pouch from one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other two hands should be free to make equal; and instruct the patient to relax his jaw muscles and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the physician sets it equal, until it recovers to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is returned with difficulty, especially when the two jawbones are together, if they have been loosened by hot water and oil, so that you return them slightly; do not force the return, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the patient's mouth is well moistened, he puts a damp cloth on his forehead made of rose oil and wax, then binds it lightly with soft threads; and the patient sleeps on his back, with his legs between two cushions, so that he does not move to the right or left, nor makes an effort to speak, but takes light food until the pains are gone, and the jawbones are numb; and then eats what he wants lightly, and does not trouble himself to open his mouth to eat or drink, until the jawbone is well numbed and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be brought back to their point within an hour, and are not converted to their places, then fever and habitual sweats come, and perhaps colic, and perhaps vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a death sentence; and many times the person dies from whom it happens, within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the shoulder
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The shoulder cannot be dislocated from inside the chest towards the back and in a continuous motion of the shoulder blade and the ribcage, and is sometimes dislocated to the rear, and one can feel this well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back, stretches out his arms; and then presses strongly on the joint with his palm, and it will return; then puts on the poultice and bandage, and tightens it; and the shoulder that was dislocated in the back cannot come loose; if it does not, and if it comes loose at any time, he must be reset to its place, as we have said; then puts on the poultice and bandage, and tightens it, and instructs the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus the shoulder of the spine is restored when it has come out of its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	The shoulder is not dislocated except in three ways: the one that dislocates towards the armpit below; and the second that dislocates towards the back; and by chance it dislocates above, and this happens rarely; and does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor does it dislocate inwardly for the armlets; and more often dislocates downwards towards the armpit, especially in those who have little flesh, for then it springs forth hastily; and in those who have enough flesh, it jumps a little, and returns a little.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men that they receive a blow or crushing, and the shoulder becomes swollen with a hot abscess, and thinks that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary that you examine it thoroughly, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that dislocation occurs when it falls towards the armpit, and makes a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them a manifest diversity; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a pit, and below the armpit touching the top of the shoulder, just like an ox; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their neck or move it with any movements; and likewise, if it is dislocated upwards, then it is not hidden, for you can see it manifestly when you touch; and this kind of dislocation is not cured except by returning, when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the attendants lift the patient's hand up high, then put their fingers below the socket, and lift the jointure up to its place by force; and the attendants lift the hand again, and stretch it up high, then put it back down; so it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	Et s'elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l'assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l'espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu'il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s'espaule desoz l'assele dou malaide, et lieve l'assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l'ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then they can carry with them something heavy, and the dislocation will come back now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And one also remedies it in another way: and this is how one drives a long iron rod into the earth, so that the head is as steady as a piston, and not too thick or too thin; then place it under the patient, but only if they have draped themselves softly above, and the patient is standing at the length of the wood; then stretch out their hand down below to one side, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, do this treatment: take a rod with two arms and four prongs wide, which has a handle rounded so as to fit easily into a hole in the ashes, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie soft cloths on top of the stick so that the stick does not hurt the patient, then place it below the socket of the patient's shoulder; and stretch one arm up over the long rod, and tie the assistant on the rod, and the arm at the head of the hand, then put the arm on a shelf of a wide basket, and let the hands down, and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is applied, in whatever manner it may be, you should place below the armpit an equal wool sphere, then put the plaster on top of powder from the mill, with incense and egg yolk, on all the shoulder and around, then strain below the armpit properly, and turn the string over the plaster, and bind the hand to one's neck, and let the remaining hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he massage little, until the member is comforted, for it will heal sooner; and then massage more after five days or seven, and move him; and if it is firm and not softened, then it is sound.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come in, or for another reason, then it is necessary that you administer cauterizations to three apertures, as it is written before this chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and after seven days it dislocates again, and the joint does not hold and cannot lift its arm above, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the breast, or shoulders, or back, is made by impulse and stretching of hands, and it should be treated in another way; and care for it until it is sound.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes swelling in the member and delayed movement, then the patient should take baths many times, until that swelling is alleviated, and returns to its original nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the hip
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the hip is displaced in a way, and comes back in a way; and is displaced from all sides, and just as much before and behind, and the dislocation is not returned, for one sees it well and feels it well; and displaces according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the cut patient with the healthy one, so it can be seen clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is broken, and cannot bend the arm, nor reach its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it so that the abscess does not come to life, for if the abscess were to come to life, it would be grievous to reset; and perhaps it cannot be completely reset from top to bottom, especially when it is in the back; thus it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and perhaps death comes.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such that when it can be reset, you should stretch his hand to your two hands; and his arms be spread out, and the hands of the mire according to the hip around, above, and below, and bind the joint to its shoulders together, or to the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his own hand, and fixes at the root of the palm the hip which is displaced.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it will not return to its place, administer strong extension; and this is because two ministers should stretch the arm, and hold it on both sides, so that it does not move in extension; then turn the arm from each side, when you have wrapped a double, long, and wide cloth around it; and when the surgeon has joined the jointure to her hand, she should oil it with some oil to soften the jointure, then bind the jointure firmly, until it recovers; and when it is at rest, put on dry powder with egg, and bind it firmly, and let the arm hang at the patient's neck, and leave it for a few days, then release.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then release the string, and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, then reapply the plaster and the string, and leave it thus for a few days, until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	Et if he feels grievance after the setting of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and rub well, and press until he is soothed; or you put a sheep's fat snow on the jointure, then leave for one day and one night, then remove, and make him enter the bath; and when he sweats, then rub the jointure temperately, then put the snow back on, and then enter the bath; and thus do two or three times, until he is healed; and if you see, then put a moist heated wort of valerian on top, and strain it on; so he will return to his disposition.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is displaced and returns lightly, more than other joints. Nevertheless, it is necessary to reset it quickly, in the same place where it was displaced, so that the swelling subsides or an abscess does not form hotly.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the setting is that you put the sick hand on a board, and stretch out the fingers of your hand, and put it equal with the eyes, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the jointure, and sets it so that it recovers; however, you must look to see if it is well in place; then put the patient's back hand on a board for stretching and setting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then the patient places their back of hand on the table, and the assistant places their hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, it's good. But if not, then one applies soothing poultices to abscesses and leaves them in this way without starting again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place after some days, then the twisted joint remains; and no harm comes to the patient except that their hand is numb, and they cannot exert any strength at all: then know that the nerves are pinched, or the arteries; thus there is no other remedy than to force it back into place by a fire cautery in this case, and perhaps nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when his hands are back in place, put on the plaster that we have said, then bind and leave it for five days, then release it and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well and there is some swelling, then soak it in hot water, and rub it gently until he is sound.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on each side, or at the back of the palm or in the wrist; then the finger is bent and forced into its original position as much as possible, then hold the tip of the finger and guide it towards the part where it was disjoined; and leave it for two days, and then set it straight that day; and bind it with a splint, as we have said, and release it by day, and make it move, and bind it again to the splint; and do this often until it is straight, and do so also if it is dislocated at the wrist of the hand, and do so too when it is dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the spine
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine or neck is dislocated, or there are multiple dislocations, there is no remedy, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	Et li signes si est that the evacuations jump forth without will, nor can they be held, and many times some member is softened, or both thighs or two arms or one; and often the shinbone becomes four parts; that which becomes last is called "gilbositez"; the cure is that you reward if the gilbositez has come from childhood: if there is no cure nor healing for all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or beatings or similar things, the old manner of cures by great words say it is not at all in great benefit; but I have abbreviated it according to my intention and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the gilbositeit that comes to the belly before, there is no remedy nor health; and similarly that which comes directly on both sides, and one cannot cure those fires except the proper one that comes to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient be stretched out on his face in one place equal, and have restraint below him, so he does not bleed; then put two tissons in the earth firmly, and another between the armpits of the patient, and at the hips, and at the knees; and two ministers know how to tie the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the two tissons; and be well closed, the tissons as we have said, and the midwife put her palms on the spine firmly, until it revives.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, then take a board three arm-lengths long, and hollow out the bottom part, and the patient should be in the side position, and push the head of the board onto the lower part, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and set the mirrors at the feet onto the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see, do it on the turntable that turns with the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And it is that you place two pokers at the head of the patient one arm-length apart, and two others towards the feet, with a palm's width between each poker, above and below; and in each poker, have one perforation where the turntable turns, and the pokers should be firmly on the ground so they do not move; and between each pair of pokers, have one turning poker, which is for turning the turntable, and in two turnings, have two small pokers one palm-length apart, to turn the turntable; and then tie the strap that is among the assemblages at the head turntable towards the head, and the other strap towards the feet on the other turntable, and each servant turns their turntable all along the strap, and the master sets the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, and puis les estoupes, and puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, and use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; and s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; and aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, and aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, and cuide on que ce soit dislocations; and c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.
des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder do not come except from dislocation alone, nor does it come as with other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to three parts: within and without, and before and behind; and more so within than without, and less so before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of his dislocation is that when one joins the afflicted leg with a healthy one, it is longer, and apart more shows the patient's knee than the healthy one, and the patient cannot double his kneecap on fire; and is the skin which is below swollen abscesses hot, because the head of the thigh bone comes away.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes from behind is that this accident is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of him to whom it comes from before is that his leg is well-shaped according to its completion; however, he does not flex his kneecap without pain, and if one wants him to walk, he cannot at first, and holds back his urine, and swells with anger, and when he walks, he passes over the ankle.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of him to whom it comes from behind is that he cannot stretch his kneecap nor flex it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the anger is softened, and the head of the thigh bone is in the place under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this likeness of dislocation are that you correct if the dislocation is ancient and it remains according to its condition, there being no remedy; and there is no need for one to have presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the one whose dislocation is fresh, and it is of three kinds of dislocations, you must hasten to turn the joint, and stretch it within and without, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return to its place, and there is no need for another remedy.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, it is necessary that you appear as a strong minister, and hold the leg firmly with both hands, or at the joint where it is attached to the knee; and another minister stretches his hand upwards in such a way that he places his hands under his armpits, then tightens a soft ligament above the thigh; and one other takes hold of the head of the ligament; and all stretch up and down at once, until the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains thus.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to three similar things, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	Se ceu non, if not
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot bind it in this manner as we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong soft rope on both heels and legs, and the afflicted leg should be stretched two digits more than the others; then hang it from the head of a tree, and place it on top of the earth two arm's length; then command one servant to grasp the chief of the groin, and have another servant standing with the patient who grasps firmly the groin, for the jointure returns now hastily.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is at its farthest point, then the patient lies down as we have said in those with gilbositeit, and stretch the rope on the afflicted leg properly, and also on the hip; then put two brands, one at the head and another at the heels, then thrust the brand between the patient's thighs into the form; and have damp cloths planted around, so that the patient does not get hurt, then have each servant approach him, and the physician place an equal distance from his hand to the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If she returns, it's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place him on the table and press thus as we have said in the Gilboisheit, and position the patient on the holy coast.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is before, then it is necessary to stretch out the diseased leg quickly, and according to what I have said; and put the barber's hand on top of the diseased angle, then press with the other hand, and stretch down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the back, it's not necessary to stretch the patient down or lift him up on the earth, but rather let him be as if his hip were dislocated at the back, as we have said about lying on two hips; and lie on his face, and extend the bandage as we have said before, and should press on the joint at the table; and it will be just so when the patient stretches out his legs, and they are even; then adjust the thighs, put the poultice, and strain with a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and let him rest for three days or four, then loosen, and put the poultice on; and if you see that they are even, strain again as before, and leave it for three days; then loosen, and make him walk well, until the limbs are comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three manners: that is to say, inward and outward, and behind; and does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	Et the sign is that you command the patient to bend his leg at his hip, and if it does not bend at his hip, know that he is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and draw it between your thighs, then bend both sides of the knee firmly; and one other minister extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he bends his leg at his hip slightly; and apply the plaster, and make the leg comfortable at the hip, and secure them together strongly for three or four days, then release him; and do not trouble the patient with walking, until the limbs are comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not straight, administer strong stretching, as we have said in the treatment of the gout, until it is sound.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the ankle
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The ankle is sometimes sprained and sometimes fully dislocated, inwardly and outwardly.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and tend towards the part where it is dislocated: the reduction is easy, and one must stretch gently with their hands when it is simply felt.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is fully reduced, it is necessary that you make the patient stand upright, and hold the assistants except by the leg, above the ankle; then take the foot to your right hand, and then to your left hand twice, then stretch upwards, and gently push the foot up; and do this two times, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is well; if not, then begin again, for it will return; and if it cannot return thus, make the patient sit on his back on the ground, and place a strap firmly in the earth between his thighs, and bind cloths around, so that the patient does not get hurt; then hold the assistants at the thigh, and another assistant stretches out the foot to your hands or to a cord, which is tied above the foot of the calf; then stretch each assistant evenly, and the straps should be placed between the patient's thighs to retain the patient when you are stretching; then place the mirrors equally on the dislocation in your hands, and another assistant holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is set, so put the poultice and bandages on top, and strain firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the ankle behind, lest the bandage be too tight; then let it stay for two or three days, and if the bandage loosens, re-tie it; then release it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient to walk for four days; and if he walks before that term, it is not sure that it will not relapse.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses appear there, it is necessary to heal them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	you must
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the joints are relaxed, you should stretch them gently without effort, and it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any notch of the heel or back of the foot, it is necessary that you make the patient sit on a flat seat or on .ie. table straight away, and put your foot on what appears to be the joint, then press firmly with your foot until it realigns; and when it is even, and there is no more deformity, so place a board under the sole of the foot at two feet, then tie firmly, and let it stay for three days, then release it; and make him rest, until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la veut restorer, maintes fois advient que le malade meurt: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, si tu n'es sage en l'art et tu ne l'as usé longtemps, et si tu n'es pitieux et miséricordieux et tardif, ne mie hardi; et use au commencement de choses apaisantes apostème chaud, et laisse le malade en la main Dieu, si tu ne vois espérance de santé; et quant tu i vois espérance, si ramènes maintenant le membre au lieu, ainsois que l'apostème chaude vienne; et quant les membres sont à lieu, si administre choses apaisantes apostème chaud, et cure la plaie, si comme il convient, d'oignemens dessicats; et si avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus désevrés, si les otes, et fais ce que nous avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d'entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j'ai dit, car cela te vaut moult selonc ton Créateur, et pour la saveté de ton arme et de ton corps.
